10085-8{_}2873{_}What prodigies he wrought in war's red field!
10085-8{_}2874{_}He showed himself ahead of all his peers.
10085-8{_}2875{_}A blood-mare was his mother.
10085-8{_}2876{_}He excelled   In all the contests 'twixt the wandering camps;   I tourneyed with him careless of my fate.

10085-8{_}2887{_}Each day my heart burns fiercer, and my joy   Has fled away.
10085-8{_}2888{_}Now tell me, O my eyes,   Why shed so many tears?
10085-8{_}2889{_}Beyond a doubt   The pleasures of the world will capture you.
10085-8{_}2890{_}And will you grant no mercy?
10085-8{_}2891{_}My sad soul   But sees its torments grow.

10085-8{_}2893{_}I do but weep   And my head whitens for the beauteous one,   With pearly teeth.
10085-8{_}2894{_}My eyes no longer can   Endure the separation from their friend.
10085-8{_}2895{_}The sun that lights us to the zenith climbs,   Then gains the west.
10085-8{_}2896{_}It disappears from sight   When it has gained the summit of the vault   Celestial.

10085-8{_}2898{_}To these would I compare the lovely queen   Of all this age, the daughter of Ahmed,   Descendant of a race illustrious,   The daughter of Donaonda.

10085-8{_}2904{_}She's worth a hundred steeds of noble race,   A thousand camels, and a grove of palms   In Zyban.
10085-8{_}2905{_}Yes, all Djryd is she worth,   From near to far.

10085-8{_}2907{_}The treasurer of all riches is she worth,   My black-eyed beauty.

10085-8{_}3116{_}Thy remedy is lost, my good Lord Taleb.
10085-8{_}3117{_}Pray God for me, O Taleb, I implore.
10085-8{_}3118{_}But how to cure the malady of love?
10085-8{_}3119{_}There is no remedy, and all is lost.
10085-8{_}3120{_}I die for lack of strength to bear my trials.
10085-8{_}3121{_}It is to thee that I intrust myself,   The healer who must bring rest to my heart;   For now a living brand burns in my breast.
10085-8{_}3122{_}If thou art skilful, find a cure for me.
10085-8{_}3123{_}[1] This elegy is the work of a celebrated sheik of Tlemcen, Mahomet-Ben-Sahla, whose period was the first half of the eighteenth century.
10085-8{_}3124{_}He left a son, Ben Medien, a poet, too, and his descendants still live, near Tlemcen, in a village called Feddan-es-Seba.
10085-8{_}3125{_}Look in thy book and calculate for me   If thou canst quench the burning brand within.
10085-8{_}3126{_}I will become thy slave, and thou may'st keep   Me or at auction sell.
10085-8{_}3127{_}Where is thy cure!
10085-8{_}3128{_}Thy remedy is lost, my good Lord Taleb.
10085-8{_}3129{_}The Taleb looked at me and said: "Take heart,   O lover, courage!
10085-8{_}3130{_}Thou hast sipped, I see,   The cup of death already, and thou hast   Not long to live.
10085-8{_}3131{_}But hear my counsel now.
10085-8{_}3132{_}Have patience!
10085-8{_}3133{_}Tis the only thing that will   Sustain thee.
10085-8{_}3134{_}Thou shalt thus obtain the gifts   Of Him who only knows thy future days.
10085-8{_}3135{_}Thy fate shall be unrolled according to   The will of God, the sovereign Lord most high.
10085-8{_}3136{_}"Turn to thy God.
10085-8{_}3137{_}Beseech him constantly.
10085-8{_}3138{_}He hears with mercy and he knows all souls.
10085-8{_}3139{_}He turns away no one who comes to him.
10085-8{_}3140{_}He sees the bottom of their hearts, and lists.
10085-8{_}3141{_}Bear his decrees with patience camels show.
10085-8{_}3142{_}They walk from land to land and hope to lose   At last their burdens."

10085-8{_}3147{_}My punishment too long has lasted.
10085-8{_}3148{_}I   Am tired of waiting.
10085-8{_}3149{_}Never was adventure   More strange than mine.

10085-8{_}3170{_}And, oh, how grows my love!

10085-8{_}3201{_}THE CITY GIRL AND THE COUNTRY GIRL    O thou who hearest me, I will recite   One of these stories I am master of--   A tale that's true.
10085-8{_}3202{_}By these I move the hearts   Of lovers like to thee, and I divert   Their minds with pleasant stories.
10085-8{_}3203{_}As I hear,   So I relate them, and they please my friends,   By flow of wit and eloquence of thought.
10085-8{_}3204{_}I tell of beauties' battle.
10085-8{_}3205{_}And my song   Is written in perfection, straight and clear.
10085-8{_}3206{_}Thinking of naught I walked along one day   When I had gone to see some beauties fair   Whose like I ne'er have seen in city nor   In country yet.
10085-8{_}3207{_}I should have said   That they were sun and moon, and that the girls   Of that time were bright stars surpassing far   The Pleiades.
10085-8{_}3208{_}The stars are envious   In their far firmaments, each of   The other.
10085-8{_}3209{_}That's the reason why we see   Eclipses of the sun and moon.
10085-8{_}3210{_}My tale   Is true.
10085-8{_}3211{_}The women, like unto the stars,   Are jealous also.
10085-8{_}3212{_}Two young virgins met   The day I saw them, a sad day for them,   For one was jealous of the other one.
10085-8{_}3213{_}The citizeness said to the Bedouine:   "Look at thy similars and thou shalt see   In them but rustics, true dogs of the camp.
10085-8{_}3214{_}Now what art thou beside a city girl?
10085-8{_}3215{_}Thou art a Bedouine.
10085-8{_}3216{_}Dost thou not dream   Of goat-skin bottles to be filled at dawn?
10085-8{_}3217{_}And loads of wood that thou must daily cut?
10085-8{_}3218{_}And how thou'rt doomed to turn the mill all night,   Fatigued, harassed?
10085-8{_}3219{_}Thy feet, unshod, are chapped   And full of cracks.
10085-8{_}3220{_}Thy head can never feel   The solace of uncovering, and thou,   All broken with fatigue, must go to sleep   Upon the ground, in soot and dust to lie,   Just like a serpent coiled upon himself.
10085-8{_}3221{_}Thy covering is the tatters of old tents,   Thy pillow is the stones upon the hearth.
10085-8{_}3222{_}All clad in rags thou hast a heavy sleep   Awaking to another stupid day.
10085-8{_}3223{_}Such is the life of all you country folk.
10085-8{_}3224{_}What art thou then compared to those who live   In shade of walls, who have their mosques for prayer   Where questions are discussed and deeds are drawn?"
10085-8{_}3225{_}The Arab woman to the city girl   Replied: "Get out!
10085-8{_}3226{_}Thou'rt like a caverned owl.
10085-8{_}3227{_}And who art thou beside the Arab girls,   The daughters of those tribes whose standards wave   Above brave bands of horsemen as they speed?
10085-8{_}3228{_}Look at thy similars.
10085-8{_}3229{_}The doctor ne'er   Can leave their side.
10085-8{_}3230{_}Without an illness known   They're faded, pale, and sallow.
10085-8{_}3231{_}The harsh lime   Hath filled thy blood with poison.
10085-8{_}3232{_}Thou art dead,   Although thou seem'st alive.
10085-8{_}3233{_}Thou ne'er hast seen   Our noble Arabs and their feats of strength,   Who to the deserts bring prosperity   By their sharp swords!
10085-8{_}3234{_}If thou could'st see our tribe   When all the horsemen charge a hostile band,   Armed with bright lances and with shields to break   The enemy's strong blow!
10085-8{_}3235{_}Those who are like   To them are famed afar and glorified.
10085-8{_}3236{_}They're generous hosts and men of nature free.
10085-8{_}3237{_}Within the mosques they've built and lodgings made   For _tolba_ and for guests.
10085-8{_}3238{_}All those who come   To visit them, bear gifts away, and give   Them praises.
10085-8{_}3239{_}Why should they reside in town   Where everything's with price of silver bought?"
10085-8{_}3240{_}The city girl replied: "Oh, Bedouine,   Thou dost forget all that thou hast to do.
10085-8{_}3241{_}Thou go'st from house to house, with artichokes   And mallows, oyster-plants, and such,   Thy garments soaked all through and through with grease.
10085-8{_}3242{_}This is thy daily life.
10085-8{_}3243{_}I do not speak   Of what is hid from view.
10085-8{_}3244{_}Thy slanders cease!
10085-8{_}3245{_}What canst thou say of me?
10085-8{_}3246{_}Better than thee   I follow all the precepts of the Sonna   And note more faithfully the sacred hours.
10085-8{_}3247{_}Hid by my veil no eye hath seen my face:   I'm not like thee, forever in the field.
10085-8{_}3248{_}I've streets to go on when I walk abroad.
10085-8{_}3249{_}What art thou, then, beside me?
10085-8{_}3250{_}I heard not   The cows and follow them about all day.
10085-8{_}3251{_}Thou eatest sorrel wild and heart of dwarf   Palm-tree.
10085-8{_}3252{_}Thy feet are tired with walking far,   And thy rough hands with digging in the earth."
10085-8{_}3253{_}"Now what impels you, and what leads you on,"   The country girl of city girl inquired,   "To outrage us like this and say such words   Against us, you who are the very worst   Of creatures, in whom all the vices are   Assembled?
10085-8{_}3254{_}You are wicked sinners all,   And Satan would not dare to tell your deeds.
10085-8{_}3255{_}You are all witches.
10085-8{_}3256{_}And you would betray   Your brother, not to speak of husbands.
10085-8{_}3257{_}You   Walk all unguarded in the street alone,   Against your husband's will.
10085-8{_}3258{_}And you deny   Your holy faith.
10085-8{_}3259{_}The curse of heav'n will weigh   Upon you when you go to meet your God.
10085-8{_}3260{_}Not one of you is honest.
10085-8{_}3261{_}O ye blind   Who do not wish to see, whence comes your blindness?
10085-8{_}3262{_}You violate the law divine, and few   Among you fear the Lord.
10085-8{_}3263{_}'Tis in the country,   Amid the fields, that women worship God.
10085-8{_}3264{_}Why say'st thou that the city women sole   Are pious?
10085-8{_}3265{_}Canst thou say my prayers for me?"
10085-8{_}3266{_}"What pleasure have the country girls?"
10085-8{_}3267{_}replied   The city girl.
10085-8{_}3268{_}"They've no amusements there.
10085-8{_}3269{_}There's nothing to divert the eyes.
10085-8{_}3270{_}Their hands   They do not stain with henna, setting off   A rounded arm.
10085-8{_}3271{_}Rich costumes they wear not,   Which cost some hundred silver pieces each,   Nor numerous garments decked with precious stones.
10085-8{_}3272{_}They are not coifed with kerchiefs of foulard   With flowers brocaded.
10085-8{_}3273{_}Neither have they veils   Nor handkerchiefs of silk and broidered gold.
10085-8{_}3274{_}They never have a negress nurse to bring   Their children up and run on services   Throughout the house.
10085-8{_}3275{_}And yet they boast as loud   As any braggart.
10085-8{_}3276{_}Why bring'st thou the charge   That I a blameful life do lead, whilst thine   Deserves reproof?
10085-8{_}3277{_}Dirt in the country holds   Supreme control.
10085-8{_}3278{_}The water's scarce enough   To drink, with none left for the bath.
10085-8{_}3279{_}The ground   Serves you as bed, and millet is your food,   Or rotten wheat and barley."
10085-8{_}3280{_}Then took up   The word, and spoke the Arab woman dark:   "Who are thy ancestors?
10085-8{_}3281{_}Which is thy tribe   Among all those that fill the mighty world?
10085-8{_}3282{_}You're only Beny Leqyt, and the scum   Of people of all sorts.
10085-8{_}3283{_}Thou call'st thyself   A city woman.
10085-8{_}3284{_}What are city men?
10085-8{_}3285{_}Thy lords don't slander folk.
10085-8{_}3286{_}'Tis only those   Who come whence no one knows who have so rude   A tongue.
10085-8{_}3287{_}Thou wouldst insult me, thou, of stock   Like thine, with such a name abroad!
10085-8{_}3288{_}And thou   Wouldst taunt a Qorechyte, a Hachemite   Of glorious ancestors who earned their fame.
10085-8{_}3289{_}Tis proper for a woman born of such   A stock illustrious to vaunt herself   Upon her origin.
10085-8{_}3290{_}But thou, a vile   Descendant of a conquered race!
10085-8{_}3291{_}"Thou call'st   Thyself a Sunnite, yet thou knowest not   The three great things their Author gave to us:   (He knows all secrets.)
10085-8{_}3292{_}First is Paradise,   Then the Koran, and then our Prophet great,   Destroyer of false faiths and for all men   The interceder.
10085-8{_}3293{_}Whosoe'er loves him   Doth love the Arabs, too, and cleaves to them.
10085-8{_}3294{_}And whosoe'er hates them hates, too, in truth,   The chosen one of God.
10085-8{_}3295{_}Thou hatest him,   For thou revil'st my ancestors, and seek'st   To lower their rank and vilify their fame.
10085-8{_}3296{_}Think on thine evil deeds, against the day   When in thy grave thou'lt lie, and that one, too,   When thou shalt rise again, insulter of   The Arabs, king of peoples on the earth."
10085-8{_}3297{_}"The Arabs I do not at all despise,"   The city woman said, "nor yet decry   Their honor, and 'tis only on account   Of thee I spoke against them.
10085-8{_}3298{_}But 'tis thou   Who hast insulted all my family, and placed   Thy race above.
10085-8{_}3299{_}He who begins is e'er   At fault, and not the one who follows.
10085-8{_}3300{_}Thou   The quarrel didst commence.
10085-8{_}3301{_}Pray God, our Lord,   To pardon me, as I will pray him, too,   And I the Arabs will no more attack.
10085-8{_}3302{_}If they offend me I will pardon them   And like them for our holy prophet's sake.
10085-8{_}3303{_}I shall awake in Paradise some day.
10085-8{_}3304{_}From them 'tis given, far beyond all price.
10085-8{_}3305{_}Frankly, I love them more than I do love   Myself.
10085-8{_}3306{_}I love them from my very heart.
10085-8{_}3307{_}He who a people loveth shall arise   With them.
10085-8{_}3308{_}And here's an end to all our words   Of bickering and mutual abuse."
10085-8{_}3309{_}I told them that it was my duty plain   To reconcile them.
10085-8{_}3310{_}I accorded both   Of them most pure intentions.
10085-8{_}3311{_}Then I sent   Them home, and made agreeable the way.
10085-8{_}3312{_}Their cares I drove away with honeyed words.
10085-8{_}3313{_}I have composed the verses of this piece,   With sense more delicate than rare perfume   Of orange-flower or than sugar sweet,   For those kind hearts who know how to forgive.
10085-8{_}3314{_}As for the evil-minded, they should feel   The _zeqqoum_.
10085-8{_}3315{_}With the flowers of rhetoric   My song is ornamented: like the breast   Of some fair virgin all bedecked with stones   Which shine like bright stars in the firmament.
10085-8{_}3316{_}Some of its words will seem severe to those   Who criticise.
10085-8{_}3317{_}I culled them like unto   A nosegay in the garden of allusions.
10085-8{_}3318{_}May men of lion hearts and spirit keen--   Beloved by God and objects of his care--   Receive my salutations while they live,   My countless salutations.
10085-8{_}3319{_}I should let   My name be known to him who's subject to   The Cherfa and obeys their mighty power.
10085-8{_}3320{_}The _mym_ precedes, then comes the written _ha_.
10085-8{_}3321{_}The _mym_ and _dal_ complete the round and make   It comprehensible to him who reads   Mahomet.
10085-8{_}3322{_}May God pardon me this work   So frivolous, and also all my faults   And errors.
10085-8{_}3323{_}I place confidence in him,   Creator of all men, with pardon free   For all our sins, and in his mercy trust,   Because he giveth it to him who seeks.
10085-8{_}3324{_}The country girl and city girl appeared   Before the judge, demanding sentence just.
10085-8{_}3325{_}In fierce invectives for a while they joined,   But after all I left them reconciled.
10085-8{_}3326{_}POPULAR TALES OF THE BERBERS  [_Translated by René Basset and Chauncey C. Starkweather_]    STORIES OF ANIMALS    THE TURTLE, THE FROG, AND THE SERPENT  Once upon a time the turtle married a frog.
10085-8{_}3327{_}One day they quarrelled.
10085-8{_}3328{_}The frog escaped and withdrew into a hole.
10085-8{_}3329{_}The turtle was troubled and stood in front of his door very much worried.
10085-8{_}3330{_}In those days the animals spoke.
10085-8{_}3331{_}The griffin came by that way and said: "What is the matter with you?
10085-8{_}3332{_}You look worried this morning."
10085-8{_}3333{_}"Nothing ails me," answered the turtle, "except that the frog has left me."
10085-8{_}3334{_}The griffin replied, "I'll bring him back."
10085-8{_}3335{_}"You will do me a great favor."
10085-8{_}3336{_}The griffin took up his journey and arrived at the hole of the frog.
10085-8{_}3337{_}He scratched at the door.
10085-8{_}3338{_}The frog heard him and asked, "Who dares to rap at the door of a king's daughter?"
10085-8{_}3339{_}"It is I, the griffin, son of a griffin, who lets no carrion escape him."
10085-8{_}3340{_}"Get out of here, among your corpses.
10085-8{_}3341{_}I, a daughter of the King, will not go with you."
10085-8{_}3342{_}He departed immediately.
10085-8{_}3343{_}The next day the vulture came along by the turtle and found it worrying before its door, and asked what was the trouble.
10085-8{_}3344{_}It answered: "The frog has gone away."
10085-8{_}3345{_}"I'll bring her back," said the vulture.
10085-8{_}3346{_}"You will do me a great favor."
10085-8{_}3347{_}The vulture started, and reaching the frog's house began to beat its wings.
10085-8{_}3348{_}The frog said: "Who conies to the east to make a noise at the house of the daughter of kings, and will not let her sleep at her ease?"
10085-8{_}3349{_}"It is I, the vulture, son of a vulture, who steals chicks from under her mother."
10085-8{_}3350{_}The frog replied: "Get away from here, father of the dunghill.
10085-8{_}3351{_}You are not the one to conduct the daughter of a king."
10085-8{_}3352{_}The vulture was angry and went away much disturbed.
10085-8{_}3353{_}He returned to the turtle and said: "The frog refuses to come back with me.
10085-8{_}3354{_}Seek someone else who can enter her hole and make her come out.
10085-8{_}3355{_}Then I will bring her back even if she won't walk."
10085-8{_}3356{_}The turtle went to seek the serpent, and when he had found him he began to weep.
10085-8{_}3357{_}"I'm the one to make her come out," said the serpent.
10085-8{_}3358{_}He quickly went before the hole of the frog and scratched at the door.
10085-8{_}3359{_}"What is the name of this other one?"
10085-8{_}3360{_}asked the frog.
10085-8{_}3361{_}"It is I, the serpent, son of the serpent.
10085-8{_}3362{_}Come out or I'll enter."
10085-8{_}3363{_}"Wait awhile until I put on my best clothes, gird my girdle, rub my lips with nut-shells, put some _koheul_ in my eyes; then I will go with you."
10085-8{_}3364{_}"Hurry up," said the serpent.
10085-8{_}3365{_}Then he waited a little while.
10085-8{_}3366{_}Finally he got angry, entered her house, and swallowed her.
10085-8{_}3367{_}Ever since that time the serpent has been at war with the frog.
10085-8{_}3368{_}Whenever he sees one he chases her and eats her.
10085-8{_}3369{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE HEDGEHOG, THE JACKAL, AND THE LION  Once upon a time the jackal went in search of the hedgehog and said to it: "Come along.
10085-8{_}3370{_}I know a garden of onions.
10085-8{_}3371{_}We will fill our bellies."
10085-8{_}3372{_}"How many tricks have you?"
10085-8{_}3373{_}asked the hedgehog.
10085-8{_}3374{_}"I have a hundred and one."
10085-8{_}3375{_}"And I," said the other, "have one and a half."
10085-8{_}3376{_}They entered the garden and ate a good deal.
10085-8{_}3377{_}The hedgehog ate a little and then went to see if he could get out of the entrance or not.
10085-8{_}3378{_}When he had eaten enough so that he could just barely slip out, he stopped eating.
10085-8{_}3379{_}As for the jackal, he never stopped eating until he was swollen very much.
10085-8{_}3380{_}As these things were going on, the owner of the garden arrived.
10085-8{_}3381{_}The hedgehog saw him and said to his companion:  "Escape!
10085-8{_}3382{_}the master is coming."
10085-8{_}3383{_}He himself took flight.
10085-8{_}3384{_}But in spite of his exhortations the jackal couldn't get through the opening.
10085-8{_}3385{_}"It is impossible," he said.
10085-8{_}3386{_}"Where are those one hundred and one tricks?
10085-8{_}3387{_}They don't serve you now."
10085-8{_}3388{_}"May God have mercy on your parents, my uncle, lend me your half a trick."
10085-8{_}3389{_}"Lie down on the ground," answered the hedgehog.
10085-8{_}3390{_}"Play dead, shut your mouth, stretch out your paws as if you were dead, until the master of the garden shall see it and cast you into the street, and then you can run away."
10085-8{_}3391{_}On that the hedgehog departed.
10085-8{_}3392{_}The jackal lay down as he had told him until the owner of the garden came with his son and saw him lying as if dead.
10085-8{_}3393{_}The child said to his father:  "Here is a dead jackal.
10085-8{_}3394{_}He filled his belly with onions until he died."
10085-8{_}3395{_}Said the man, "Go, drag him outside."
10085-8{_}3396{_}"Yes," said the child, and he took him and stuck a thorn into him.
10085-8{_}3397{_}"Hold on, enough!"
10085-8{_}3398{_}said the jackal.
10085-8{_}3399{_}"They play with reeds, but this is not sport."
10085-8{_}3400{_}The child ran to his father and said, "The jackal cried out, 'A reed!

10085-8{_}3403{_}"Why do you tell me that it still lives?"
10085-8{_}3404{_}"It surely does."

10085-8{_}3407{_}The child went to his father.

10085-8{_}3411{_}Immediately the animal jumped up and started to run away.

10085-8{_}3413{_}The jackal took them, put them on, and departed.

10085-8{_}3445{_}The lion remained and did as his companion had told him.

10085-8{_}3489{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE STOLEN WOMAN  It is related that a man of the Onlad Draabad married his cousin, whom he loved greatly.
10085-8{_}3490{_}He possessed a single slave and some camels.
10085-8{_}3491{_}Fearing lest someone should carry off his wife on account of her beauty, he resolved to take her to a place where no one should see her.
10085-8{_}3492{_}He started, therefore, with his slave, his camels, and his wife, and proceeded night and day until he arrived at the shore of the great salt sea, knowing that nobody would come there.
10085-8{_}3493{_}One day when he had gone out to see his camels and his slave, leaving his wife alone in the tent, she saw a ship that had just then arrived.
10085-8{_}3494{_}It had been sent by a sultan of a far country, to seek in the islands of the salt sea a more beautiful wife for him than the women of his land.
10085-8{_}3495{_}The woman in the tent, seeing that the ship would not come first to her, went out first in front.
10085-8{_}3496{_}The people said to her, "Come on board in order to see the whole ship."
10085-8{_}3497{_}She went aboard.
10085-8{_}3498{_}Finding her to be just the one for whom they were seeking, they seized her and took her to their Sultan.
10085-8{_}3499{_}On his return, the husband, not finding his wife, realized that she had been stolen.
10085-8{_}3500{_}He started to find the son of Keij, the Christian.
10085-8{_}3501{_}Between them there existed a friendship.
10085-8{_}3502{_}The son of Keij said to him: "Bring a ship and seven men, whose guide I will be on the sea.
10085-8{_}3503{_}They need not go astray nor be frightened.
10085-8{_}3504{_}The city is three or four months' journey from here."
10085-8{_}3505{_}They set sail in a ship to find the city, and were on the way the time that he had said.
10085-8{_}3506{_}Arriving they cast their anchor near the city, which was at the top of a high mountain.
10085-8{_}3507{_}Their chief went ashore and saw a fire lighted by someone.
10085-8{_}3508{_}He went in that direction.
10085-8{_}3509{_}It was an old woman, to whom he told his story.
10085-8{_}3510{_}She gave him news of his wife.
10085-8{_}3511{_}They agreed to keep silence between themselves.
10085-8{_}3512{_}Then the old woman added: "In this place there are two birds that devour people.
10085-8{_}3513{_}At their side are two lions like to them, and two men.
10085-8{_}3514{_}All of these keep guard over your wife."
10085-8{_}3515{_}He bought a sheep, which he killed; then he went to the two birds and threw them a part of it.
10085-8{_}3516{_}While they were quarrelling over it he passed by them and came near to the two lions, to which he did the same.
10085-8{_}3517{_}Approaching the two men, he found them asleep.
10085-8{_}3518{_}He went as far as the place where his wife was in prison, and attracted her attention by scratching her foot.
10085-8{_}3519{_}He was disguised and said to her, "I have sought you to tell you something."
10085-8{_}3520{_}He took her by the hand.
10085-8{_}3521{_}They both went out, and he swore that if she made the slightest noise he would kill her.
10085-8{_}3522{_}He also asked her which was the swiftest boat for the journey.
10085-8{_}3523{_}She pointed out the best boat there, and they embarked in it.
10085-8{_}3524{_}There were some stones on board, and when he threw one at a ship it was crushed from stem to stern, and all on board perished.
10085-8{_}3525{_}He started to find the son of Keij.
10085-8{_}3526{_}While they were at sea a marine monster swallowed them and the ship on which they were sailing.
10085-8{_}3527{_}The chief took some pitch and had it boiled in a kettle.
10085-8{_}3528{_}The monster cast up the ship on the shore of the sea.
10085-8{_}3529{_}They continued their journey, proceeding by the seaside.
10085-8{_}3530{_}Behold one day they came to a deserted city.
10085-8{_}3531{_}They desired to take what it contained of riches, silver, and gold.
10085-8{_}3532{_}All of a sudden the image of an armed man appeared to them.
10085-8{_}3533{_}They could not resist or kill him at first, but finally they destroyed him and took all the riches of the houses.
10085-8{_}3534{_}When they arrived near the son of Keij he said to them: "I want only the ship."
10085-8{_}3535{_}So the other man took the treasures and returned home with his wife.
10085-8{_}3536{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE KING, THE ARAB, AND THE MONSTER  In former times there was a king of the At Taberchant (the son of a negress), whose city was situated at the foot of a mountain.
10085-8{_}3537{_}An enormous beast came against them, entered the city, and devoured all the people.
10085-8{_}3538{_}The beast established itself in the city and stayed there a century.
10085-8{_}3539{_}One day it was hungry.
10085-8{_}3540{_}It came out into the plain, found some Arabs with their tents, their sheep, their oxen, their mares, and their camels.
10085-8{_}3541{_}The beast fell upon them in the night and ate them all up, leaving the earth all white with their bones; then it went back to the city.
10085-8{_}3542{_}A single man escaped, thanks to his good mare.
10085-8{_}3543{_}He arrived at a city of the At Taberchant and, starving, began to beg.
10085-8{_}3544{_}The King of the Jews said to him: "Whence do you come into our country--you who invoke the lord of men [Mahomet]?
10085-8{_}3545{_}You don't know where you are.
10085-8{_}3546{_}We are Jews.
10085-8{_}3547{_}If you will embrace our religion, we will give you food."
10085-8{_}3548{_}"Give me some food," said the Arab, "and I will give you some good advice."
10085-8{_}3549{_}The King took him to his house and gave him some supper, and then asked him what he had to say.
10085-8{_}3550{_}"An enormous monster has fallen upon us," said the Arab.
10085-8{_}3551{_}"It ate up everybody.
10085-8{_}3552{_}I will show you its city.
10085-8{_}3553{_}It has two gates, one at the north and the other at the south."
10085-8{_}3554{_}"To-morrow," said the King.
10085-8{_}3555{_}When he awoke the next day, they mounted horses and followed the way to the gate of the monster's city.
10085-8{_}3556{_}They looked at it and went away.
10085-8{_}3557{_}"What shall we do?"
10085-8{_}3558{_}said the King.
10085-8{_}3559{_}"Let us make a great trap of the size of the entrance to the city, at the southern gate.
10085-8{_}3560{_}At the northern gate we will place a forty-mule load of yellow sulphur.
10085-8{_}3561{_}We will set it on fire, and then escape and see what will happen."
10085-8{_}3562{_}"Your advice is good," said the King.
10085-8{_}3563{_}They returned to the city of the Jews, ordered the smiths to make a big trap and commanded the citizens to furnish the sulphur.
10085-8{_}3564{_}When all was ready, they loaded the mules, went to the monster's city, set the trap at the southern gate, and at the northern they placed the sulphur, which they set on fire, and then fled.
10085-8{_}3565{_}The monster came out by the southern gate.
10085-8{_}3566{_}Half of his body was caught in the trap that the two men had set.
10085-8{_}3567{_}He was cut in two, filling the river with blood.
10085-8{_}3568{_}The King and the Arab entered the city and found a considerable treasure, which they removed in eighty loads to the city of the Jews.
10085-8{_}3569{_}When they had got back to the palace the King said to his companion: "Be my caliph.
10085-8{_}3570{_}My fortune and thine shall be the same."
10085-8{_}3571{_}They sat down and had supper.
10085-8{_}3572{_}The prince put in the stew some poison and turned it to the Arab.
10085-8{_}3573{_}The latter observed what he had done and said, "Where did that bird come from?"
10085-8{_}3574{_}When the King of the Jews raised his head to look, the Arab turned the dish around, placing the poison side of it in front of the King.
10085-8{_}3575{_}He did not perceive the trick, and died on the spot.
10085-8{_}3576{_}The Arab went to the gate of the city and said to the inhabitants: "I am your King.
10085-8{_}3577{_}You are in my power.
10085-8{_}3578{_}He who will not accept my religion, I will cut off his head."
10085-8{_}3579{_}They all embraced Islamism and practised fasting and prayer.
10085-8{_}3580{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE LION, THE JACKAL, AND THE MAN  In times past, when the animals spoke, there existed, they say, a laborer who owned a pair of oxen, with which he worked.
10085-8{_}3581{_}It was his custom to start out with them early in the morning, and in the evening he returned with one ox.
10085-8{_}3582{_}The next day he bought another and went to the fallow land, but the lion came and took one ox from him and left him only one.
10085-8{_}3583{_}He was in despair, seeking someone to advise him, when he met the jackal and told him what had taken place between him and the lion.
10085-8{_}3584{_}The jackal demanded:  "What will you give me if I deliver you from the lion?"
10085-8{_}3585{_}"Whatever you wish I will give it to you."
10085-8{_}3586{_}"Give me a fat lamb," answered the jackal.
10085-8{_}3587{_}"You will follow my advice.

10085-8{_}3589{_}I will arrive on that hill on the other side.

10085-8{_}3591{_}you must answer, 'It is an ass which I have taken with me to carry barley.'
10085-8{_}3592{_}I will say to you, 'I am looking for the lion, and not for an ass,' Then he will ask you, 'Who is speaking to you?'
10085-8{_}3593{_}Answer him, 'It is the nems!'

10085-8{_}3596{_}Then I will continue: 'I have not heard very well.
10085-8{_}3597{_}Strike him again once more until he shall really be dead,'" The next day he came to him as before to eat an ox.
10085-8{_}3598{_}When the jackal saw him he called his friend and said, "Who is that with you?"
10085-8{_}3599{_}"It is a beaver which is before me."
10085-8{_}3600{_}The jackal answered: "Where is the lion?
10085-8{_}3601{_}I am looking for him."
10085-8{_}3602{_}"Who is talking to you?"
10085-8{_}3603{_}asked the lion, of the laborer.
10085-8{_}3604{_}"The 'nems.'"
10085-8{_}3605{_}"Hide me," cried the lion, "for I fear him."
10085-8{_}3606{_}The laborer said to him, "Stretch yourself out before me, shut your eyes, and don't move."
10085-8{_}3607{_}The lion stretched out before him, shut his eyes, and held his breath.
10085-8{_}3608{_}The peasant said to the jackal, "I have not seen the lion pass to-day."

10085-8{_}3610{_}"It is a beaver."
10085-8{_}3611{_}"Take your axe," said the jackal, "and strike that beaver."
10085-8{_}3612{_}The laborer obeyed and struck the lion violently between the eyes.
10085-8{_}3613{_}"Strike hard," said the jackal again; "I did not hear very well."
10085-8{_}3614{_}He struck him three or four times more, until he had killed him.
10085-8{_}3615{_}Then he called the jackal: "See, I have killed him.
10085-8{_}3616{_}Come, let me embrace you for your good advice.

10085-8{_}3618{_}They separated and each went his way.
10085-8{_}3619{_}As for the peasant, the next day, as soon as dawn, he took a lamb, put it into a sack, tied it up, went into the court-yard and hung it up.
10085-8{_}3620{_}Then while he went to get his oxen to till his fields, at that moment, his wife opened the sack, set the lamb free, and replaced it by a dog.
10085-8{_}3621{_}The peasant took the sack and went to his work.
10085-8{_}3622{_}He attached his oxen and set to work, till the arrival of the jackal.
10085-8{_}3623{_}The jackal said to him, "Where is that promise you made me?"

10085-8{_}3625{_}Open it and you'll find the lamb which I give you."

10085-8{_}3627{_}"How have I deceived you?"
10085-8{_}3628{_}asked the other.
10085-8{_}3629{_}"As for the lamb, I put him in the sack.
10085-8{_}3630{_}Open it well; I do not lie."
10085-8{_}3631{_}The jackal followed his advice, he opened the sack, a dog jumped fiercely out.
10085-8{_}3632{_}When the jackal saw the dog he ran away, but the dog caught him and ate him up.
10085-8{_}3633{_}*       *       *       *       *   SALOMON AND THE GRIFFIN  Our Lord Salomon was talking one day with the genii.
10085-8{_}3634{_}He said to them: "There is born a girl at Dabersa and a boy at Djaberka.
10085-8{_}3635{_}This boy and this girl shall meet," he added.
10085-8{_}3636{_}The griffin said to the genii: "In spite of the will of the divine power, I shall never let them meet each other."
10085-8{_}3637{_}The son of the King of Djaberka came to Salomon's house, but hardly had he arrived when he fell ill; then the griffin carried away the daughter of the King of Djaberka and put her upon a big tree at the shore of the sea.
10085-8{_}3638{_}The wind impelled the prince, who had embarked.
10085-8{_}3639{_}He said to his companions, "Put me ashore."
10085-8{_}3640{_}He went under the big tree and fell asleep.
10085-8{_}3641{_}The young girl threw leaves at him.
10085-8{_}3642{_}He opened his eyes, and she said to him: "Beside the griffin, I am alone here with my mother.
10085-8{_}3643{_}Where do you come from?"
10085-8{_}3644{_}"From Djaberka."
10085-8{_}3645{_}"Why," she continued, "has God created any human beings except myself, my mother, and our Lord Salomon?"
10085-8{_}3646{_}He answered her, "God has created all kinds of human beings and countries."
10085-8{_}3647{_}"Go," she said, "bring a horse and kill it.
10085-8{_}3648{_}Bring also some camphor to dry the skin, which you will hang on the top of the mast."
10085-8{_}3649{_}The griffin came, and she began to cry, saying, "Why don't you conduct me to the house of our Lord Salomon?"
10085-8{_}3650{_}"To-morrow I will take you."
10085-8{_}3651{_}She said to the son of the King, "Go hide inside the horse."
10085-8{_}3652{_}He hid there.
10085-8{_}3653{_}The next day the griffin took away the carcass of the horse, and the young girl departed also.
10085-8{_}3654{_}When they arrived at the house of our Lord Salomon, the latter said to the griffin, "I told you that the young girl and the young man should be united."
10085-8{_}3655{_}Full of shame the griffin immediately fled and took refuge in an island.
10085-8{_}3656{_}*       *       *       *       *   ADVENTURE OF SIDI MAHOMET   One day Mouley Mahomet summoned Sidi Adjille to come to Morocco, or he would put him in prison.
10085-8{_}3657{_}The saint refused to go to the city until the prince had sent him his chaplit and his "dalil" as pledges of safety.
10085-8{_}3658{_}Then he started on the way and arrived at Morocco, where he neither ate nor drank until three days had passed.
10085-8{_}3659{_}The Sultan said to him:  "What do you want at my palace?
10085-8{_}3660{_}I will give it to you, whatever it may be."
10085-8{_}3661{_}Sidi Adjille answered, "I ask of you only one thing, that is, to fill with wheat the feed-bag of my mule."
10085-8{_}3662{_}The prince called the guardian, and said to him, "Fill the feed-bag of his mule."
10085-8{_}3663{_}The guardian went and opened the door of the first granary and put wheat in the feed-bag until the first granary was entirely empty.
10085-8{_}3664{_}He opened another granary, which was soon equally exhausted, then a third, and so on in this fashion until all the granaries of the King were emptied.
10085-8{_}3665{_}Then he wanted to open the silos, but their guardian went and spoke to the Sultan, together with the guardian of the granaries.
10085-8{_}3666{_}"Lord," they said, "the royal granaries are all empty, and yet we have not been able to fill the feed-bag of the saint's mule."
10085-8{_}3667{_}The donkey-drivers came from Fas and from all countries, bringing wheat on mules and camels.
10085-8{_}3668{_}The people asked them,  "Why do you bring this wheat?"
10085-8{_}3669{_}"It is the wheat of Sidi Mahomet Adjille that we are taking."
10085-8{_}3670{_}The news came to the King, who said to the saint, "Why do you act so, now that the royal granaries are empty?"
10085-8{_}3671{_}Then he called together the members of his council and wanted to have Sidi Mahomet's head cut off.
10085-8{_}3672{_}"Go out," he said to him.
10085-8{_}3673{_}"Wait till I make my ablutions" [for prayer], answered the saint.
10085-8{_}3674{_}The people of the makhzen who surrounded him watched him among them, waiting until he had finished his ablutions, to take him to the council of the King and cut off his head.
10085-8{_}3675{_}When Sidi Mahomet had finished washing, he lifted his eyes to heaven, got into the tub where was washing, and vanished completely from sight.
10085-8{_}3676{_}When the guardians saw that he was no longer there, they went vainly to continue the search at his house at Tagountaft.
10085-8{_}3677{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE HAUNTED GARDEN  A man who possessed much money had two daughters.
10085-8{_}3678{_}The son of the caliph of the King asked for one of them, and the son of the cadi asked for the other, but their father would not let them marry, although they desired it.
10085-8{_}3679{_}He had a garden near his house.
10085-8{_}3680{_}When it was night, the young girls went there, the young men came to meet them, and they passed the night in conversation.
10085-8{_}3681{_}One night their father saw them.
10085-8{_}3682{_}The next morning he killed his daughters, buried them in his garden, and went on a pilgrimage.
10085-8{_}3683{_}That lasted so until one night the son of the cadi and the son of the caliph went to a young man who knew how to play on the flute and the rebab.
10085-8{_}3684{_}"Come with us," they said to him, "into the garden of the man who will not give us his daughters in marriage.
10085-8{_}3685{_}You shall play for us on your instruments."
10085-8{_}3686{_}They agreed to meet there that night.
10085-8{_}3687{_}The musician went to the garden, but the two young men did not go.
10085-8{_}3688{_}The musician remained and played his music alone.
10085-8{_}3689{_}In the middle of the night two lamps appeared, and the two young girls came out of the ground under the lamps.
10085-8{_}3690{_}They said to the musician: "We are two sisters, daughters of the owner of the garden.
10085-8{_}3691{_}Our father killed us and buried us here.
10085-8{_}3692{_}You, you are our brother for this night.
10085-8{_}3693{_}We will give you the money which our father has hidden in three pots.
10085-8{_}3694{_}Dig here," they added.
10085-8{_}3695{_}He obeyed, found the three pots, took them away, and became rich, while the two girls returned to their graves.
10085-8{_}3696{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE WOMAN AND THE FAIRY  A woman who was named Omm Halima went one day to the stream to wash at the old spring.
10085-8{_}3697{_}Alone, in the middle of the day, she began her work, when a woman appeared to her and said: "Let us be friends, you and I, and let us make a promise.
10085-8{_}3698{_}When you come to this spring, bring me some herma and perfumes.
10085-8{_}3699{_}Cast them into the fountain which faces the qsar.
10085-8{_}3700{_}I will come forth and I will give you money."
10085-8{_}3701{_}And so the wife of Ben Sernghown returned every day and found the other woman, who gave her pieces of money.
10085-8{_}3702{_}Omm Khalifah was poor.
10085-8{_}3703{_}When she "became friends" with the fairy she grew rich all of a sudden.
10085-8{_}3704{_}The people were curious to know how she had so quickly acquired a fortune.
10085-8{_}3705{_}There was a rich man, the possessor of much property.
10085-8{_}3706{_}He was called Mouley Ismail.
10085-8{_}3707{_}They said to Omm Khalifah:  "You are the mistress of Mouley Ismail, and he gives you pieces of money."
10085-8{_}3708{_}She answered, "Never have I been his mistress."
10085-8{_}3709{_}One day, when she went to the spring to bathe, the people followed her until she arrived.
10085-8{_}3710{_}The fairy came to meet her as usual, and gave her money.
10085-8{_}3711{_}The people surprised them together.
10085-8{_}3712{_}But the fairy never came out of the fountain again.
10085-8{_}3713{_}*       *       *       *       *   HAMED-BEN-CEGGAD   There was in a city a man named Hamed-ben-Ceggad.
10085-8{_}3714{_}He lived alone with his mother.
10085-8{_}3715{_}He lived upon nothing but the chase.
10085-8{_}3716{_}One day the inhabitants of the city said to the King:  "Hamed-ben-Ceggad is getting the better of you."
10085-8{_}3717{_}He said to them, "Tell me why you talk thus to me, or I will cut off your heads."
10085-8{_}3718{_}"As he only eats the flesh of birds, he takes advantage of you for his food."
10085-8{_}3719{_}The King summoned Hamed and said to him, "You shall hunt for me, and I will supply your food and your mother's, too."
10085-8{_}3720{_}Every day Hamed brought game to the prince, and the prince grew very proud of him.
10085-8{_}3721{_}The inhabitants of the city were jealous of him, and went to the Sultan and said: "Hamed-ben-Ceggad is brave.
10085-8{_}3722{_}He could bring you the tree of coral-wood and the palm-tree of the wild beasts."
10085-8{_}3723{_}The King said to him, "If you are not afraid, bring me the tree of coral-wood and the palm-tree of the wild beasts."
10085-8{_}3724{_}"It is well," said Hamed.
10085-8{_}3725{_}And the next day he took away all the people of the city.
10085-8{_}3726{_}When he came to the tree, he killed all the wild beasts, cut down the palm-tree, loaded it upon the shoulders of the people, and the Sultan built a house of coral-wood.
10085-8{_}3727{_}Seeing how he succeeded in everything, they said to the King, "Since he achieves all that he attempts, tell him to bring you the woman with the set of silver ornaments."
10085-8{_}3728{_}The prince repeated these words to Hamed, who said:  "The task you give me is harsh, nevertheless I will bring her to you," He set out on the way, and came to a place where he found a man pasturing a flock of sheep, carrying a millstone hanging to his neck and playing the flute.
10085-8{_}3729{_}Hamed said to him: "By the Lord, I cannot lift a small rock, and this man hangs a millstone to his neck."
10085-8{_}3730{_}The shepherd said: "You are Hamed-ben-Ceggad, who built the house of coral-wood?"
10085-8{_}3731{_}"Who told you?"
10085-8{_}3732{_}"A bird that flew into the sky."
10085-8{_}3733{_}He added, "I will go with you."
10085-8{_}3734{_}"Come," said Hamed.
10085-8{_}3735{_}The shepherd took the millstone from his neck, and the sheep were changed into stones.
10085-8{_}3736{_}On the way they met a naked man, who was rolling in the snow.
10085-8{_}3737{_}They said [to themselves], "The cold stings us, and yet that man rolls in the snow without the cold killing him."
10085-8{_}3738{_}The man said to them, "You are Hamed-ben-Ceggad, who built the house of coral-wood?"
10085-8{_}3739{_}"Who told you that?"
10085-8{_}3740{_}"A bird that passed flying in the sky told me.
10085-8{_}3741{_}I will accompany you."
10085-8{_}3742{_}"Come," said Hamed.
10085-8{_}3743{_}After they had pursued their way some time, they met a man with long ears.
10085-8{_}3744{_}"By the Lord," they said, "we have only small ears, and this man has immense ones."
10085-8{_}3745{_}"It is the Lord who created them thus, but if it pleases God I will accompany you, for you are Hamed-ben-Ceggad."
10085-8{_}3746{_}They arrived at the house of the woman with the silver ornaments, and Hamed said to the inhabitants, "Give us this woman, that we may take her away."
10085-8{_}3747{_}"Very well," said her brother, the ogre.
10085-8{_}3748{_}They killed an ox, placed it upon a hurdle, which they lifted up and put down with the aid of ninety-nine men.
10085-8{_}3749{_}"Give us one of your men who can lift this hurdle."
10085-8{_}3750{_}He who wore millstones hanging from his neck said, "I can lift it."
10085-8{_}3751{_}When he had placed it on the ground, they served a _couscous_ with this ox.
10085-8{_}3752{_}The ogre said, "Eat all that we give you."
10085-8{_}3753{_}They ate a little, and the man with the long ears hid the rest of the food.
10085-8{_}3754{_}The brother continued: "You give us one of you who will go to gather a branch of a tree that stands all alone on the top of a mountain two days' march in the snow."
10085-8{_}3755{_}The one who had rolled in the snow departed, and brought back the branch.
10085-8{_}3756{_}"There remains one more proof," said the ogre.
10085-8{_}3757{_}"A partridge is flying in the sky; let one of you strike it."
10085-8{_}3758{_}Hamed-ben-Ceggad killed it.
10085-8{_}3759{_}They gave him the woman, but before her departure her brother gave her a feather and said to her, "When anyone shall try to do anything to you against your will, cast this feather on the hearth and we will come to you."
10085-8{_}3760{_}People told the woman, "The old Sultan is going to marry you."
10085-8{_}3761{_}She replied, "An old man shall never marry me," and cast the feather into the fire.
10085-8{_}3762{_}Her brother appeared, and killed all the inhabitants of the city, as well as the King, and gave the woman to Hamed-ben-Ceggad.
10085-8{_}3763{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE MAGIC NAPKIN   A taleb made a proclamation in these terms: "Is there anyone who will sell himself for 100 mitquals?"
10085-8{_}3764{_}A man agreed to sell himself.
10085-8{_}3765{_}The stranger took him to the cadi, who wrote out the bill of sale.
10085-8{_}3766{_}He took the 100 mitquals and gave them to his mother and departed with the taleb.
10085-8{_}3767{_}They went to a place where the latter began to repeat certain formulas.
10085-8{_}3768{_}The earth opened and the man entered it.
10085-8{_}3769{_}The other said to him, "Bring me the candlestick of reed and the box."
10085-8{_}3770{_}He took this and came out keeping it in his pocket.
10085-8{_}3771{_}"Where is the box?"
10085-8{_}3772{_}asked the taleb.
10085-8{_}3773{_}"I did not find it."
10085-8{_}3774{_}"By the Lord, let us go."
10085-8{_}3775{_}He took him to the mountains, cast a stone at him, and went away.
10085-8{_}3776{_}He lay on the ground for three days.
10085-8{_}3777{_}Then he came to himself, went back to his own country, and rented a house.
10085-8{_}3778{_}He opened the box, found inside a silk napkin, which he opened, and in which he found seven folds.
10085-8{_}3779{_}He unfolded one.
10085-8{_}3780{_}Genii came around the chamber, and a young girl danced until the day dawned.
10085-8{_}3781{_}The man stayed there all that day until night.
10085-8{_}3782{_}The King came out that night, and, hearing the noise of the dance, he knocked at the door, with his vezir.
10085-8{_}3783{_}They received him with a red _h'aik._ He amused himself until the day dawned.
10085-8{_}3784{_}Then he went home with his vezir.
10085-8{_}3785{_}The latter sent for the man and said, "Give me the box which you have at home."
10085-8{_}3786{_}He brought it to the King, who said to him: "Give me the box which you have so that I may amuse myself with it, and I will marry you to my daughter."
10085-8{_}3787{_}The man obeyed and married the Sultan's daughter.
10085-8{_}3788{_}The Sultan amused himself with the box, and after his death his son-in-law succeeded him.
10085-8{_}3789{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE CHILD AND THE KING OF THE GENII  There was a sheik who gave instruction to two talebs.
10085-8{_}3790{_}One day they brought to one of them a dish of _couscous_ with meat.
10085-8{_}3791{_}The genius stole him and bore him away.
10085-8{_}3792{_}When they had arrived down there he taught him.
10085-8{_}3793{_}One day the child was crying.
10085-8{_}3794{_}The King of the genii asked him, "Why do you cry?"
10085-8{_}3795{_}"I am crying for my father and my mother.
10085-8{_}3796{_}I don't want to stay here any longer."
10085-8{_}3797{_}The King asked his sons, "Who will take him back?"
10085-8{_}3798{_}"I," said one of them; "but how shall I take him back?"
10085-8{_}3799{_}"Carry him back after you have stuffed his ears with wool so that he shall not hear the angels worshipping the Lord."
10085-8{_}3800{_}They had arrived at a certain place, the child heard the angels worshipping the Lord, and did as they did.
10085-8{_}3801{_}His guide released him and he remained three days without awaking.
10085-8{_}3802{_}When he came to himself, he took up his journey and found a mother-dog which slept while her little ones barked, although yet unborn.
10085-8{_}3803{_}He proceeded and met next an ass attacked by a swarm of flies.
10085-8{_}3804{_}Further on he saw two trees, on one perched a blue bird.
10085-8{_}3805{_}Afterward it flew upon the other tree and began to sing.
10085-8{_}3806{_}He found next a fountain of which the bottom was of silver, the vault of gold and the waters white.
10085-8{_}3807{_}He went on and met a man who had been standing for three days without saying a word.
10085-8{_}3808{_}Finally he arrived at a village protected by God, but which no one entered.
10085-8{_}3809{_}He met a wise man and said to him:  "I want to ask you some questions."
10085-8{_}3810{_}"What do you wish to ask me?"
10085-8{_}3811{_}"I found a mother-dog which was asleep while her little ones were barking, although yet unborn."
10085-8{_}3812{_}The sage answered, "It is the good of the world that the old man should keep silence because he is ashamed to speak."
10085-8{_}3813{_}"I saw an ass attacked by a swarm of flies."
10085-8{_}3814{_}"It is Pjoudj and Madjoudj of God (Gog and Magog) and the Antichrist."
10085-8{_}3815{_}"I met two trees, a blue bird perched on one, then flew upon the other and began to sing."
10085-8{_}3816{_}"It is the picture of the man who has two wives.
10085-8{_}3817{_}When he speaks to one the other gets angry."
10085-8{_}3818{_}"I saw a fountain of which the bottom was of silver, the vault of gold, and the waters white."
10085-8{_}3819{_}"It is the fountain of life; he who drinks of it shall not die."
10085-8{_}3820{_}"I found a man who was praying.
10085-8{_}3821{_}I stayed three days and he did not speak."
10085-8{_}3822{_}"It is he who never prayed upon the earth and is now making amends."
10085-8{_}3823{_}"Send me to my parents," concluded the child.
10085-8{_}3824{_}The old man saw a light cloud and said to it, "Take this human creature to Egypt."
10085-8{_}3825{_}And the cloud bore him to his parents.
10085-8{_}3826{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE SEVEN BROTHERS   Here is a story that happened once upon a time.
10085-8{_}3827{_}A man had seven sons who owned seven horses, seven guns, and seven pistols for hunting.
10085-8{_}3828{_}Their mother was about to increase the family.
10085-8{_}3829{_}They said to their father: "If we have a little sister we shall remain.
10085-8{_}3830{_}If we have a little brother we shall go."
10085-8{_}3831{_}The woman had a little boy.
10085-8{_}3832{_}They asked, "Which is it?"
10085-8{_}3833{_}"A boy."
10085-8{_}3834{_}They mounted their horses and departed, taking provisions with them.
10085-8{_}3835{_}They arrived at a tree, divided their bread, and ate it.
10085-8{_}3836{_}The next day they started and travelled as far as a place where they found a well, from which they drew water.
10085-8{_}3837{_}The older one said, "Come, let us put the young one in the well."
10085-8{_}3838{_}They united against him, put him in, and departed, leaving him there.
10085-8{_}3839{_}They came to a city.
10085-8{_}3840{_}The young man remained some time in the well where they had put him, until one day a caravan passing that way stopped to draw water.
10085-8{_}3841{_}While the people were drinking they heard something moving at the bottom of the well.
10085-8{_}3842{_}"Wait a moment," they said; they let down a rope, the young man caught it and climbed up.
10085-8{_}3843{_}He was as black as a negro.
10085-8{_}3844{_}The people took him away and sold him to a man who conducted him to his house.
10085-8{_}3845{_}He stayed there a month and became white as snow.
10085-8{_}3846{_}The wife of the man said:  "Come, let us go away together."
10085-8{_}3847{_}"Never!"
10085-8{_}3848{_}he answered.
10085-8{_}3849{_}At evening the man returned and asked, "What is the negro doing?"
10085-8{_}3850{_}"Sell him," said the woman.
10085-8{_}3851{_}He said, "You are free.
10085-8{_}3852{_}Go where you please."
10085-8{_}3853{_}The young man went away and came to a city where there was a fountain inhabited by a serpent.
10085-8{_}3854{_}They couldn't draw water from this fountain without his eating a woman.
10085-8{_}3855{_}This day it was the turn of the King's daughter to be eaten.
10085-8{_}3856{_}The young man asked her:  "Why do you weep?"
10085-8{_}3857{_}"Because it is my turn to be devoured to-day."
10085-8{_}3858{_}The stranger answered, "Courage, I will kill the serpent, if it please God."
10085-8{_}3859{_}The young girl entered the fountain.
10085-8{_}3860{_}The serpent darted toward her, but as soon as he showed his head the young man struck it with his stick and made it fly away.
10085-8{_}3861{_}He did the same to the next head until the serpent was dead.
10085-8{_}3862{_}All the people of the city came to draw water.
10085-8{_}3863{_}The King said:  "Who has done this?"
10085-8{_}3864{_}"It is he," they cried, "the stranger who arrived yesterday."
10085-8{_}3865{_}The King gave him his daughter and named him his lieutenant The wedding-feast lasted seven days.
10085-8{_}3866{_}My story is finished before my resources are exhausted.
10085-8{_}3867{_}*       *       *       *       *   HALF-A-COCK   In times past there was a man who had two wives, and one was wise and one was foolish.
10085-8{_}3868{_}They owned a cock in common.
10085-8{_}3869{_}One day they quarrelled about the cock, cut it in two, and each took half.
10085-8{_}3870{_}The foolish wife cooked her part.
10085-8{_}3871{_}The wise one let her part live, and it walked on one foot and had only one wing.
10085-8{_}3872{_}Some days passed thus.
10085-8{_}3873{_}Then the half-a-cock got up early, and started on his pilgrimage.
10085-8{_}3874{_}At the middle of the day he was tired and went toward a brook to rest.
10085-8{_}3875{_}A jackal came there to drink.
10085-8{_}3876{_}Half-a-Cock jumped on his back, stole one of his hairs, which it put under its wing and resumed its journey.
10085-8{_}3877{_}It proceeded until evening and stopped under a tree to pass the night there.
10085-8{_}3878{_}It had not rested long when it saw a lion pass near the tree where it was lying.
10085-8{_}3879{_}As soon as it perceived the lion it jumped on its back and stole one of its hairs, which it put with that of the jackal.
10085-8{_}3880{_}The next morning it got up early and took up its journey again.
10085-8{_}3881{_}Arrived at the middle of a forest, it met a boar and said:  "Give me a hair from your back, as the king of the animals and the trickiest of them have done--the jackal and the lion."
10085-8{_}3882{_}The boar answered, "As these two personages so important among the animals have done this, I will also give you what you request."
10085-8{_}3883{_}He plucked a hair from his back and gave it to Half-a-Cock.
10085-8{_}3884{_}The latter went on his way and arrived at the palace of a king.
10085-8{_}3885{_}It began to crow and to say:  "To-morrow the King will die, and I will take his wife."
10085-8{_}3886{_}Hearing these words the King gave to his negroes the command to seize Half-a-Cock, and cast him into the middle of the sheep and goat-pen to be trampled upon and killed by them, so that the King might get rid of his crowing.
10085-8{_}3887{_}The negroes seized him and cast him into the pen to perish.
10085-8{_}3888{_}When he got there Half-a-Cock took from under his wing the jackal's hair and burnt it in the fire.
10085-8{_}3889{_}As soon as it was near the fire the jackal came and said:  "Why are you burning my hair?
10085-8{_}3890{_}As soon as I smelled it, I came running."
10085-8{_}3891{_}Half-a-Cock replied, "You see what situation I am in.
10085-8{_}3892{_}Get me out of it."
10085-8{_}3893{_}"That is an easy thing," said the jackal, and immediately blowed in order to summon his brothers.
10085-8{_}3894{_}They gathered around him, and he gave them this command: "My brothers, save me from Half-a-Cock, for it has a hair from my back which it has put in the fire.
10085-8{_}3895{_}I don't want to burn.
10085-8{_}3896{_}Take Half-a-Cock out of the sheep-pen, and you will be able to take my hair from its hands."
10085-8{_}3897{_}At once the jackals rushed to the pen, strangled everything that was there, and rescued Half-a-Cock.
10085-8{_}3898{_}The next day the King found his stables deserted and his animals killed.
10085-8{_}3899{_}He sought for Half-a-Cock, but in vain.
10085-8{_}3900{_}The latter, the next day at the supper hour, began to crow as it did the first time.
10085-8{_}3901{_}The prince called his negroes and said to them:  "Seize Half-a-Cock and cast him into the cattle-yard so that it may be crushed under their feet."
10085-8{_}3902{_}The negroes caught Half-a-Cock and threw him into the middle of the cow-pen.
10085-8{_}3903{_}As soon as it reached there, it took the lion's hair and put it into the fire.
10085-8{_}3904{_}The lion came, roaring, and said:  "Why do you burn my hair?
10085-8{_}3905{_}I smelled from my cave the odor of burning hair, and came running to learn the motive of your action."
10085-8{_}3906{_}Half-a-Cock answered: "You see my situation.
10085-8{_}3907{_}Help me out of it."
10085-8{_}3908{_}The lion went out and roared to call his brothers.
10085-8{_}3909{_}They came in great haste and said to him, "Why do you call us now?"
10085-8{_}3910{_}"Take the Half-a-Cock from the ox-yard, for it has one of my hairs, which it can put into the fire.
10085-8{_}3911{_}If you don't rescue Half-a-Cock, it will burn the hair, and I don't want to smell the odor of burning hair while I am alive."
10085-8{_}3912{_}His brothers obeyed.
10085-8{_}3913{_}They at once killed all the cattle in the pen.
10085-8{_}3914{_}The King saw that his animals were all dead, and he fell into such a rage that he nearly strangled.
10085-8{_}3915{_}He looked for Half-a-Cock to kill it with his own hands.
10085-8{_}3916{_}He searched a long time without finding it, and finally went home to rest.
10085-8{_}3917{_}At sunset Half-a-Cock came to his usual place and crowed as on the former occasions.
10085-8{_}3918{_}The King called his negroes and said to them:  "This time when you have caught Half-a-Cock, put it in a house and shut all the doors till morning.
10085-8{_}3919{_}I will kill it myself."
10085-8{_}3920{_}The negroes seized him immediately and put him in the treasure-room.
10085-8{_}3921{_}When it got there, it saw money under its feet.
10085-8{_}3922{_}It waited till it had nothing to fear from the masters of the house, who were all sound asleep, took from under its wing the hair of the boar, started a fire, and placed the hair in it.
10085-8{_}3923{_}At once the boar came running and shaking the earth.
10085-8{_}3924{_}It thrust its head against the wall.
10085-8{_}3925{_}The wall shook and half of it fell down, and going to Half-a-Cock the boar said:  "Why are you burning my hair at this moment?"
10085-8{_}3926{_}"Pardon me, you see the situation in which I am, without counting what awaits me in the morning, for the King is going to kill me with his own hands if you don't get me out of this prison."
10085-8{_}3927{_}The boar replied: "The thing is easy; fear not, I will open the door so that you may go out.
10085-8{_}3928{_}In fact, you have stayed here long enough.
10085-8{_}3929{_}Get up, go and take money enough for you and your children."
10085-8{_}3930{_}Half-a-Cock obeyed.
10085-8{_}3931{_}It rolled in the gold, took all that stuck to its wing and its foot, and swallowed as much as it could hold.
10085-8{_}3932{_}It took the road it had followed the first day and when it had arrived near the house it called the mistress and said: "Strike now, be not afraid to kill me."
10085-8{_}3933{_}His mistress began to strike until Half-a-Cock called from beneath the mat:  "Enough now.
10085-8{_}3934{_}Roll the mat."
10085-8{_}3935{_}She obeyed and saw the earth all shining with gold.
10085-8{_}3936{_}*       *       *       *       *  At the time when Half-a-Cock returned from his pilgrimage the two women owned a dog in common.
10085-8{_}3937{_}The foolish one seeing that her companion had received much money said to her:  "We will divide the dog between us."
10085-8{_}3938{_}The wise woman answered: "We can't do anything with it.
10085-8{_}3939{_}Let it live, I will give you my half.
10085-8{_}3940{_}Keep it for yourself.
10085-8{_}3941{_}I have no need of it."
10085-8{_}3942{_}The foolish one said to the dog, "Go on a pilgrimage as Half-a-Cock did and bring me some gold."
10085-8{_}3943{_}The dog started to carry out the commands of his mistress.
10085-8{_}3944{_}She began her journey in the morning and came to a fountain.
10085-8{_}3945{_}As she was thirsty she started to drink.
10085-8{_}3946{_}As she stopped she saw in the middle of the fountain a yellow stone.
10085-8{_}3947{_}She took it in her mouth and ran back home.
10085-8{_}3948{_}When she reached the house she called her mistress and said to her:  "Get ready the mats and the rods, you see that I have come back from the pilgrimage."
10085-8{_}3949{_}The foolish one prepared the mats under which the dog ran as soon as she heard the voice of her mistress and said, "Strike gently."
10085-8{_}3950{_}The woman seized the rods and struck with all the force possible.
10085-8{_}3951{_}The dog cried out to her a long while for her to stop the blows.
10085-8{_}3952{_}Her mistress refused to stop until the animal was cold.
10085-8{_}3953{_}She lighted up the mats and found the dog dead with the yellow stone in its mouth.
10085-8{_}3954{_}*       *       *       *       *   STRANGE MEETINGS  Once upon a time a man was on a journey and he met a mare who grazed in the meadow.
10085-8{_}3955{_}She was thin, lean, and had only skin and bone.
10085-8{_}3956{_}He went on until he came to a place where he found a mare which was fat, although she did not eat.
10085-8{_}3957{_}He went on further until he met a sheep which kicked against a rock till evening to pass the night there.
10085-8{_}3958{_}Advancing he met a serpent which hung in a hole from which it could not get out.
10085-8{_}3959{_}Farther on, he saw a man who played with a ball, and his children were old men.
10085-8{_}3960{_}He came to an old man who said to him:  "I will explain all that to you.
10085-8{_}3961{_}The lean mare which you saw represents the rich man whose brothers are poor.
10085-8{_}3962{_}The fat mare represents the poor man whose brothers are rich.
10085-8{_}3963{_}The serpent which swings unable to enter nor to leave the hole is the picture of the word which once spoken and heard can never go back.
10085-8{_}3964{_}The sheep which kicks against the rock to pass the night there, is the man who has an evil house.
10085-8{_}3965{_}The one whose children you saw aged while he was playing ball, what does he represent?
10085-8{_}3966{_}That is the man who has taken a pretty wife and does not grow old.
10085-8{_}3967{_}His children have taken bad ones."
10085-8{_}3968{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE KING AND HIS FAMILY   In times gone by a king reigned over Maghreb.
10085-8{_}3969{_}He had four sons.
10085-8{_}3970{_}He started, he, his wife, and his children, for the Orient.
10085-8{_}3971{_}They set sail, but their ship sank with them.
10085-8{_}3972{_}The waves bore them all in separated directions.
10085-8{_}3973{_}One wave took the wife; another bore the father alone to the middle of the sea on an island where he found a mine of silver.
10085-8{_}3974{_}He dug out enough silver until he had a great quantity and he established himself in the country.
10085-8{_}3975{_}His people after heard tell of him and learned that he dwelt in the midst of the sea.
10085-8{_}3976{_}They built houses until there was a great city.
10085-8{_}3977{_}He was king of that country.
10085-8{_}3978{_}Whoever came poor to him he gave him pieces of money.
10085-8{_}3979{_}A poor man married his wife.
10085-8{_}3980{_}As for his sons, they applied themselves to a study, each in a different country.
10085-8{_}3981{_}They all became learned men and feared God.
10085-8{_}3982{_}The King had a search made for _tolbas_ who should worship God.
10085-8{_}3983{_}The first of the brothers was recommended to him.
10085-8{_}3984{_}He sent for him.
10085-8{_}3985{_}He sought also a _khodja_.
10085-8{_}3986{_}The second brother was designated.
10085-8{_}3987{_}He summoned him to the court.
10085-8{_}3988{_}The prince also especially wanted an _adel_.
10085-8{_}3989{_}Another brother was pointed to him.
10085-8{_}3990{_}He made him come to him as, indeed, he also did the imam, who was none other than the fourth brother.
10085-8{_}3991{_}They arrived at their father's without knowing him or being known by him.
10085-8{_}3992{_}The wife and the man who had espoused her also came to the King to make complaint.
10085-8{_}3993{_}When they arrived the wife went alone that night to the palace.
10085-8{_}3994{_}The prince sent for the four _tolba_ to pass the night with him until morning.
10085-8{_}3995{_}During the; night he spied upon them to see who they were.
10085-8{_}3996{_}One of them said to the others, "Since sleep comes not upon us, let each one make known who he is."
10085-8{_}3997{_}One said: "My father was a king.
10085-8{_}3998{_}He had much money and four sons whose names were like yours."
10085-8{_}3999{_}Another said: "My father was a king.
10085-8{_}4000{_}My case is like yours."
10085-8{_}4001{_}Another said: "My father was a king.
10085-8{_}4002{_}My case is like yours."
10085-8{_}4003{_}The fourth said in his turn: "My father, too, was a king.
10085-8{_}4004{_}My case is like that of your three.
10085-8{_}4005{_}You are my brothers."
10085-8{_}4006{_}Their mother overheard them and took to weeping until day.
10085-8{_}4007{_}They took her to the prince, who said, "Why do you weep?"
10085-8{_}4008{_}She answered: "I was formerly the wife of a king and we had four sons.
10085-8{_}4009{_}We set sail, he, our children, and I.
10085-8{_}4010{_}The ship which bore us was wrecked.
10085-8{_}4011{_}Each one was borne away alone, until yesterday when they spoke before me during the night and showed me what had happened to them, to their father, and to their mother."
10085-8{_}4012{_}The King said, "Let me know your adventure."
10085-8{_}4013{_}They told him all that had happened.
10085-8{_}4014{_}Then the prince arose, weeping, and said, "You are my children," and to the woman, "You are my wife."
10085-8{_}4015{_}God reunited them.
10085-8{_}4016{_}*       *       *       *       *   BEDDOU  Two men, one of whom was named Beddou and the other Amkammel, went to market bearing a basket of figs.
10085-8{_}4017{_}They met a man who was working, and said to him:  "God assist you!"
10085-8{_}4018{_}"Amen!"
10085-8{_}4019{_}he answered.
10085-8{_}4020{_}One of them wanted to wash himself, but there was no water.
10085-8{_}4021{_}The laborer, him who was with him (_sic_), said, "What is your name?"
10085-8{_}4022{_}"Beddou."
10085-8{_}4023{_}"By the Lord, Beddou, watch my oxen while I go to drink."
10085-8{_}4024{_}"Go!"
10085-8{_}4025{_}When he had gone, he took away one of the oxen.
10085-8{_}4026{_}On his return the laborer saw that one was missing.
10085-8{_}4027{_}He went to the other traveller and asked him:  "By my father, what is your name?"
10085-8{_}4028{_}"Amkammel Ouennidhui" ("The Finisher"), he answered.
10085-8{_}4029{_}"By the Lord, Amkammel Ouennidhui, watch this ox for me while I go look for the one that is gone."
10085-8{_}4030{_}"Go!"
10085-8{_}4031{_}He stole the other one.
10085-8{_}4032{_}When the laborer returned he didn't even find the second.
10085-8{_}4033{_}The two thieves went away, taking the oxen.
10085-8{_}4034{_}They killed them to roast them.
10085-8{_}4035{_}One drank all the water of the sea, the other all the fresh water, to wash it down.
10085-8{_}4036{_}When they had finished, one stayed there to sleep, the other covered him with ashes.
10085-8{_}4037{_}The former got up to get a drink and the ashes fell on the road.
10085-8{_}4038{_}When he came back, the second covered himself with the ox-head.
10085-8{_}4039{_}His brother, who had gone to get a drink, was afraid, and ran away.
10085-8{_}4040{_}They divided the other ox to eat it.
10085-8{_}4041{_}The one who had drunk the sea-water now drank fresh water, and the one who had drunk fresh water now drank sea-water.
10085-8{_}4042{_}When they had finished their repast they took up their journey.
10085-8{_}4043{_}They found an old woman who had some money, upon which she was sitting.
10085-8{_}4044{_}When they arrived they fought.
10085-8{_}4045{_}She arose to separate them.
10085-8{_}4046{_}One of them took her place to pass the night, and pretended that he was dead.
10085-8{_}4047{_}The old woman said to him:  "Get up, my son."
10085-8{_}4048{_}He refused.
10085-8{_}4049{_}In the evening one of them stole the money, and said to his brother:  "Arise!
10085-8{_}4050{_}Let us go!"
10085-8{_}4051{_}They went away to a place where was sleeping the one who had taken the money.
10085-8{_}4052{_}The other took away the _dirkhems_ and departed, leaving the first asleep.
10085-8{_}4053{_}When he awaked he found nothing.
10085-8{_}4054{_}He started in pursuit of the other, and when he arrived he found him dying of illness.
10085-8{_}4055{_}The latter had said to his wife, "Bury me."
10085-8{_}4056{_}She buried him.
10085-8{_}4057{_}He who had first stolen the money went away.
10085-8{_}4058{_}He said, "It is an ox."
10085-8{_}4059{_}"It is I, my friend," he cried.
10085-8{_}4060{_}"Praise be to God, my friend!
10085-8{_}4061{_}May your days pass in happiness!"
10085-8{_}4062{_}Beddou said to him: "Let us go for a hunt."
10085-8{_}4063{_}They went away alone.
10085-8{_}4064{_}Beddou added: "I will shave you."
10085-8{_}4065{_}He shaved him, and when he came to the throat he killed him and buried his head.
10085-8{_}4066{_}A pomegranate-tree sprang up at this place.
10085-8{_}4067{_}One day Beddou found a fruit, which he took to the King.
10085-8{_}4068{_}When he arrived he felt that it was heavy.
10085-8{_}4069{_}It was a head.
10085-8{_}4070{_}The King asked him:  "What is that?"
10085-8{_}4071{_}"A pomegranate."
10085-8{_}4072{_}"We know what you have been doing," said the King, and had his head cut off.
10085-8{_}4073{_}My story is finished.
10085-8{_}4074{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE LANGUAGE OF THE BEASTS  Once upon a time there was a man who had much goods.
10085-8{_}4075{_}One day he went to market.
10085-8{_}4076{_}There came a greyhound, which ate some meat.
10085-8{_}4077{_}The butcher gave it a blow, which made it yelp.
10085-8{_}4078{_}Seeing this, the heart of the man was touched with compassion.
10085-8{_}4079{_}He bought of the butcher half a piece of meat and flung it to the greyhound.
10085-8{_}4080{_}The dog took it and went away.
10085-8{_}4081{_}It was the son of a king of the nether world.
10085-8{_}4082{_}Fortune changed with the man.
10085-8{_}4083{_}He lost all his possessions, and began to wash for people.
10085-8{_}4084{_}One day, he had gone to wash something, he stretched it on the sand to dry.
10085-8{_}4085{_}A jerboa appeared with a ring in its ear.
10085-8{_}4086{_}The man ran after it, killed it, hid the ring, made a fire, cooked the jerboa and ate it.
10085-8{_}4087{_}A woman came out of the earth, seized him, and demanded, "Haven't you seen my son, with an ear-ring?"
10085-8{_}4088{_}"I haven't seen anybody," he answered; "but I saw a jerboa which had a ring in its ear."
10085-8{_}4089{_}"It is my son."
10085-8{_}4090{_}She drew him under the earth and told him: "You have eaten my son, you have separated me from him.
10085-8{_}4091{_}Now I will separate you from your children, and you shall work in the place of my son."
10085-8{_}4092{_}He who was changed into a greyhound saw this man that day, and said to him: "It is you who bought some meat for a greyhound and threw it to him?"
10085-8{_}4093{_}"It is I."
10085-8{_}4094{_}"I am that greyhound.
10085-8{_}4095{_}Who brought you here?"
10085-8{_}4096{_}"A woman," answered the man, and he recounted all his adventure.
10085-8{_}4097{_}"Go and make a complaint to the King," answered the other.
10085-8{_}4098{_}"I am his son.
10085-8{_}4099{_}I'll tell him: 'This man did me a good service,' When he asks you to go to the treasure and take as much money as you wish, answer him: 'I don't want any.
10085-8{_}4100{_}I only want you to spit a benediction into my mouth,' If he asks you, 'Who told you that?'
10085-8{_}4101{_}answer, 'Nobody.'"
10085-8{_}4102{_}The man went and found the King and complained of the woman.
10085-8{_}4103{_}The King called her and asked her: "Why have you taken this man captive?"
10085-8{_}4104{_}"He ate my son."
10085-8{_}4105{_}"Why was your son metamorphosed into a jerboa?
10085-8{_}4106{_}When men see one of those they kill him and eat him."
10085-8{_}4107{_}Then addressing the man: "Give her back the ear-ring."
10085-8{_}4108{_}He gave it to her.
10085-8{_}4109{_}"Go," said the King, "take this man to the place from which you brought him."
10085-8{_}4110{_}The son of the King then said to his father: "This man did me a favor; you ought to reward him."
10085-8{_}4111{_}The King said to him: "Go to the treasure, take as much money as you can."
10085-8{_}4112{_}"I don't want money," he answered; "I want you to spit into my mouth a benediction."
10085-8{_}4113{_}"Who told you that?"
10085-8{_}4114{_}"Nobody."
10085-8{_}4115{_}"You will not be able to bear it."
10085-8{_}4116{_}"I will be able."
10085-8{_}4117{_}"When I have spat into your mouth, you will understand the language of beasts and birds; you will know what they say when they speak; but if you reveal it to the people you will die."
10085-8{_}4118{_}"I will not reveal it."
10085-8{_}4119{_}So the King spat into his mouth and sent him away, saying to the woman, "Go and take him back where you found him."
10085-8{_}4120{_}She departed, and took him back there.
10085-8{_}4121{_}He mounted his ass and came back to his house.
10085-8{_}4122{_}He arranged the load and took back to the people the linen he had washed.
10085-8{_}4123{_}Then he remounted the beast to go and seek some earth.
10085-8{_}4124{_}He was going to dig when he heard a crow say in the air:  "Dig beneath; you will sing when God has made you rich."
10085-8{_}4125{_}He understood what the crow said, dug beneath, and found a treasure.
10085-8{_}4126{_}He filled a basket with it.
10085-8{_}4127{_}On the top he put a little earth and went home, but often returned to the spot.
10085-8{_}4128{_}On one of these occasions his ass met a mule, which said:  "Are you working still?"
10085-8{_}4129{_}The ass replied: "My master has found a treasure and he is taking it away."
10085-8{_}4130{_}The mule answered: "When you are in a crowd balk and throw the basket to the ground.
10085-8{_}4131{_}People will see it, all will be discovered, and your master will leave you in peace."
10085-8{_}4132{_}The man had heard every word of this.
10085-8{_}4133{_}He filled his basket with earth only.
10085-8{_}4134{_}When they arrived at a crowd of people the ass kicked and threw the load to the ground.
10085-8{_}4135{_}Her master beat her till she had enough.
10085-8{_}4136{_}He applied himself to gathering the treasure, and became a rich merchant.
10085-8{_}4137{_}He had at home some chickens and a dog.
10085-8{_}4138{_}One day he went into the granary, and a hen followed him and ate the grain.
10085-8{_}4139{_}A cock said to her:  "Bring me a little."
10085-8{_}4140{_}She answered, "Eat for yourself."
10085-8{_}4141{_}The master began to laugh.
10085-8{_}4142{_}His wife asked him:  "What are you laughing at?"
10085-8{_}4143{_}"Nothing."
10085-8{_}4144{_}"You are laughing at me."
10085-8{_}4145{_}"Not at all."
10085-8{_}4146{_}"You must tell me what you are laughing at."
10085-8{_}4147{_}"If I tell you I shall die."
10085-8{_}4148{_}"You shall tell me, and you shall die."
10085-8{_}4149{_}"To-night."
10085-8{_}4150{_}He brought out some grain and said to his wife, "Give alms."
10085-8{_}4151{_}He invited the people, bade them to eat, and when they had gone he brought food to the dog, but he would not eat.
10085-8{_}4152{_}The neighbor's dog came, as it did every day, to eat with his dog.
10085-8{_}4153{_}To-day it found the food intact.
10085-8{_}4154{_}"Come and eat," it said.
10085-8{_}4155{_}"No," the dog answered.
10085-8{_}4156{_}"Why not?"
10085-8{_}4157{_}Then the dog told the other: "My master, hearing the chickens talk, began to laugh.
10085-8{_}4158{_}His wife asked him: 'Why are you laughing?'
10085-8{_}4159{_}'If I tell you, I shall die.'
10085-8{_}4160{_}'Tell me and die,' That is why," continued the dog, "he has given alms, for when he reveals his secret he will die, and I shall never find anyone to act as he has."
10085-8{_}4161{_}The other dog replied: "As he knows our language, let him take a stick and give it to his wife until she has had enough.
10085-8{_}4162{_}As he beats her let him say: 'This is what I was laughing at.
10085-8{_}4163{_}This is what I was laughing at.
10085-8{_}4164{_}This is what I was laughing at,' until she says to him, 'Reveal to me nothing.'"
10085-8{_}4165{_}The man heard the conversation of the dogs, and went and got a stick.
10085-8{_}4166{_}When his wife and he went to bed she said to him, "Tell me that now."
10085-8{_}4167{_}Then he took the stick and beat her, saying: "This is what I was laughing at.
10085-8{_}4168{_}This is what I was laughing at.
10085-8{_}4169{_}This is what I was laughing at," until she cried out:  "Don't tell it to me.
10085-8{_}4170{_}Don't tell it to me.
10085-8{_}4171{_}Don't tell it to me."
10085-8{_}4172{_}He left her alone.
10085-8{_}4173{_}When the dogs heard that, they rejoiced, ran out on the terrace, played, and ate their food.
10085-8{_}4174{_}From that day the wife never again said to her husband, "Tell me that!"
10085-8{_}4175{_}They lived happy ever after.
10085-8{_}4176{_}If I have omitted anything, may God forgive me for it.
10085-8{_}4177{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE APPLE OF YOUTH  There once lived a king who had five daughters and no sons.
10085-8{_}4178{_}They grew up.
10085-8{_}4179{_}He wanted them to marry, but they would not have any of the young men of the city.
10085-8{_}4180{_}A youth came from a far country and stood under the castle, beneath the window of the youngest daughter.
10085-8{_}4181{_}She saw him, and told her father she would marry him.
10085-8{_}4182{_}"Bring him in," said the King.
10085-8{_}4183{_}"He will come to-morrow."
10085-8{_}4184{_}"God be praised," said the King, "that you are pleased with us."
10085-8{_}4185{_}The young man answered, "Give me your daughter for a wife."
10085-8{_}4186{_}"Advise me," said the King.
