10085-8{_}4187{_}The stranger said, "Go and wait till to-morrow."
10085-8{_}4188{_}The next day the young man said to the King: "Make all the inhabitants of the city come out.
10085-8{_}4189{_}You will stand with the clerks at the entrance to the gate.
10085-8{_}4190{_}Dress your daughters and let them choose their husbands themselves."
10085-8{_}4191{_}The people began to come out.
10085-8{_}4192{_}The eldest daughter struck one of them on the chest with an apple, and they said: "That daughter has chosen a husband.
10085-8{_}4193{_}Bravo!"
10085-8{_}4194{_}Each one of the daughters thus selected a husband, and the youngest kept hers.
10085-8{_}4195{_}A little while afterward, the King received a visit from one of his sons-in-law, who said to him, "What do you want us to give you?"
10085-8{_}4196{_}"I'll see what my daughters want," he answered.
10085-8{_}4197{_}"Come back in six days."
10085-8{_}4198{_}When they went to see their wives the King said to them, "I will ask of you a thing about which they have spoken to me."
10085-8{_}4199{_}"What is it?
10085-8{_}4200{_}We are anxious to know."
10085-8{_}4201{_}"It is an apple, the odor of which gives to the one who breathes it youth, no matter what his age may be."
10085-8{_}4202{_}"It is difficult," they answered.
10085-8{_}4203{_}"We know not where it can be found."
10085-8{_}4204{_}"If you do not bring it to me, you cannot marry my daughter."
10085-8{_}4205{_}They kept silent, and then consulted with each other.
10085-8{_}4206{_}The youngest said to them, "Seek the means to satisfy the King."
10085-8{_}4207{_}"Give us your advice----"  "Father-in-law, to-morrow we shall bring you the apple."
10085-8{_}4208{_}His brothers-in-law added: "Go out.
10085-8{_}4209{_}To-morrow we will meet you outside the city."
10085-8{_}4210{_}The next day they all five met together.
10085-8{_}4211{_}Four of them said to the other, "Advise us or we will kill you."
10085-8{_}4212{_}"Cut off your fingers," he said.
10085-8{_}4213{_}The first one began, and the three others did the same.
10085-8{_}4214{_}The youngest one took them and put them into his game-bag, and then he added, "Wait near the city till I come back."
10085-8{_}4215{_}He went out into the desert and came to the city of the ogress.
10085-8{_}4216{_}He entered, and found her ready to grind some wheat.
10085-8{_}4217{_}He said to the ogress, "Show me the apple whose color gives eternal youth to the old man who smells it."
10085-8{_}4218{_}"You are in the family of ogres," she said.
10085-8{_}4219{_}"Cut a hair from the horse of their King.
10085-8{_}4220{_}When you go into the garden cast this hair into the fire.
10085-8{_}4221{_}You will find a tree, from which you must pick five fruits.
10085-8{_}4222{_}When plucking them do not speak a word, and keep silence on your return.
10085-8{_}4223{_}It is the smallest fruit that possesses the magic power."
10085-8{_}4224{_}He took the apple and went back to the city, where he found his companions.
10085-8{_}4225{_}He concealed in his breast the wonderful fruit, and gave the others to his brothers-in-law, one to each.
10085-8{_}4226{_}They entered the palace of the King, who was overjoyed to see them, gave them seats, and asked them, "Have you brought it or not?"
10085-8{_}4227{_}"We have brought it," they answered.
10085-8{_}4228{_}He said to the eldest, "Give me your apple first."
10085-8{_}4229{_}He took a mirror in his left hand, and the fruit in the right hand, bent down, and inhaled the odor of the apple, but without results.
10085-8{_}4230{_}He threw it down upon the ground.
10085-8{_}4231{_}The others gave him their apples, with no more success.
10085-8{_}4232{_}"You have deceived me," he said to them.
10085-8{_}4233{_}"The apples do not produce the effect that I sought."
10085-8{_}4234{_}Addressing, then, the stranger, he said, "Give me your apple."
10085-8{_}4235{_}The other son-in-law replied: "I am not of this country.
10085-8{_}4236{_}I will not give you my fruit."
10085-8{_}4237{_}"Give it to me to look at," said the King.
10085-8{_}4238{_}The young man gave it to him, saying, "Take a mirror in your right hand and the apple in your left hand."
10085-8{_}4239{_}The King put the apple to his nose, and, looking at his beard, saw that it became black.
10085-8{_}4240{_}His teeth became white.
10085-8{_}4241{_}He grew young again.
10085-8{_}4242{_}"You are my son," he said to the young man.
10085-8{_}4243{_}And he made a proclamation to his subjects, "When I am dead he shall succeed me on the throne."
10085-8{_}4244{_}His son-in-law stayed some time with him, and after the death of the King he reigned in his place and did not marry the other daughters of the King to his companions.
10085-8{_}4245{_}POPULAR TALES OF THE KABYLES  [_Translated by J. Rivière and Chauncey C. Starkweather_]    ALI AND OU ALI   Ali and Ou Ali were two friends.
10085-8{_}4246{_}One day they met at the market.
10085-8{_}4247{_}One of them bore ashes and the other carried dust.
10085-8{_}4248{_}The first one had covered his goods with a little flour.
10085-8{_}4249{_}The other had concealed his merchandise under some black figs.
10085-8{_}4250{_}"Come, I will sell you some flour," said Ali.
10085-8{_}4251{_}"Come, I will sell you some black figs," answered Ou Ali.
10085-8{_}4252{_}Each regained his own horse.
10085-8{_}4253{_}Ali, who thought he was carrying flour, found, on opening his sack, that it was only ashes.
10085-8{_}4254{_}Ou Ali, who thought he was bearing black figs, found on opening his sack that it was nothing but dust.
10085-8{_}4255{_}Another day they again greeted each other in the market.
10085-8{_}4256{_}Ali smiled.
10085-8{_}4257{_}Ou Ali smiled, and said to his friend:  "For the love of God, what is your name?"
10085-8{_}4258{_}"Ali; and yours?"
10085-8{_}4259{_}"Ou Ali."
10085-8{_}4260{_}Another time they were walking together, and said to each other:  "Let us go and steal."
10085-8{_}4261{_}One of them stole a mule and the other stole a rug.
10085-8{_}4262{_}They passed the night in the forest.
10085-8{_}4263{_}Now, as the snow was falling, Ali said to Ou Ali:  "Give me a little of your rug to cover me."
10085-8{_}4264{_}Ou Ali refused.
10085-8{_}4265{_}"You remember," he added, "that I asked you to put my rug on your mule, and you would not do it."
10085-8{_}4266{_}An instant afterward Ali cut off a piece of the rug, for he was dying of cold.
10085-8{_}4267{_}Ou Ali got up and cut the lips of the mule.
10085-8{_}4268{_}The next morning, when they awaked, Ou Ali said to Ali:  "O my dear friend, your mule is grinning."
10085-8{_}4269{_}"O my dear friend," replied Ali, "the rats have gnawed your rug."
10085-8{_}4270{_}And they separated.
10085-8{_}4271{_}Some time afterward they met anew.
10085-8{_}4272{_}Ali said to Ou Ali:  "Let us go and steal."
10085-8{_}4273{_}They saw a peasant, who was working.
10085-8{_}4274{_}One of them went to the brook to wash his cloak there, and found it dry.
10085-8{_}4275{_}He laid the blade of his sabre so that it would reflect the rays of the sun, and began to beat his cloak with his hands as if to wash it.
10085-8{_}4276{_}The laborer came to the brook also, and found the man who was washing his cloak without water.
10085-8{_}4277{_}"May God exterminate you," said he, "who wash without water."
10085-8{_}4278{_}"May God exterminate you," answered the washer, "who work without a single ox."
10085-8{_}4279{_}The other robber watched the laborer, and had already stolen one of his oxen.
10085-8{_}4280{_}The laborer went back to his plough, and said to the washer, "Keep this ox for me while I go and hunt for the other."
10085-8{_}4281{_}As soon as he was out of sight the robber took away the ox left in his charge.
10085-8{_}4282{_}The laborer returned, and seizing the goad by one end he gave a great blow on the plough-handle, crying:  "Break, now.
10085-8{_}4283{_}It matters little."
10085-8{_}4284{_}The robbers met in a wood and killed the oxen.
10085-8{_}4285{_}As they lacked salt, they went to purchase it.
10085-8{_}4286{_}They salted the meat, roasted it, and ate it.
10085-8{_}4287{_}Ali discovered a spring.
10085-8{_}4288{_}Ou Ali not being able to find water, was dying of thirst.
10085-8{_}4289{_}"Show me your spring," he said to Ali, "and I will drink."
10085-8{_}4290{_}"Eat some salt, my dear friend," answered Ali.
10085-8{_}4291{_}What could he do?
10085-8{_}4292{_}Some days afterward Ou Ali put ashes on the shoes of Ali.
10085-8{_}4293{_}The next day he followed the traces of the ashes, found the spring, and discovered thus the water that his friend was drinking.
10085-8{_}4294{_}He took the skin of one of the oxen and carried it to the fountain.
10085-8{_}4295{_}He planted two sticks above the water, hung the skin on the sticks, and placed the horns of the ox opposite the road.
10085-8{_}4296{_}During the night his friend went to the spring.
10085-8{_}4297{_}At the sight of the skin thus stretched out, fear seized him, and he fled.
10085-8{_}4298{_}"I am thirsty," said Ou Ali.
10085-8{_}4299{_}"Eat some salt, my dear friend," answered Ali, "for salt removes thirst."
10085-8{_}4300{_}Ali retired, and, after having eaten, ran to examine the skin that he had stretched out.
10085-8{_}4301{_}Ou AH ate the salt, and was dying of thirst.
10085-8{_}4302{_}"For the love of God," he said finally, "show me where you drink."
10085-8{_}4303{_}Ali was avenged.
10085-8{_}4304{_}"Come, Jew-face, and I will show you the water."
10085-8{_}4305{_}He made him drink at the spring, and said to him: "See what you were afraid of."
10085-8{_}4306{_}The meat being finished, they started away.
10085-8{_}4307{_}Ou Ali went to the house of Ali, and said to him:  "Come, we will marry you to the daughter of an old woman."
10085-8{_}4308{_}Now, the old woman had a herd of oxen.
10085-8{_}4309{_}She said to Ali: "Take this drove to the fields and mount one of the animals."
10085-8{_}4310{_}Ali mounted one of the oxen.
10085-8{_}4311{_}He fell to the ground; the oxen began to run and trample on him.
10085-8{_}4312{_}Ou Ali, who was at the house, said to the old woman:  "O my old woman, give me your daughter in marriage."
10085-8{_}4313{_}She called her daughter.
10085-8{_}4314{_}"Take a club," she said to her, "and we will give it to him until he cries for mercy."
10085-8{_}4315{_}The daughter brought a club and gave Ou AH a good beating.
10085-8{_}4316{_}Ali, who was watching the herd, came at nightfall and met his friend.
10085-8{_}4317{_}"Did the old woman accept you?"
10085-8{_}4318{_}he asked him.
10085-8{_}4319{_}"She accepted me," answered Ali.
10085-8{_}4320{_}"And is the herd easy to watch?"
10085-8{_}4321{_}"From morning till night I have nothing to do but to repose.
10085-8{_}4322{_}Take my place to-morrow, and mount one of the oxen."
10085-8{_}4323{_}The next day Ou Ali said to the old woman, "To-day I will take care of the herd."
10085-8{_}4324{_}And, on starting, he recommended Ali to ask the old woman for her daughter's hand.
10085-8{_}4325{_}"It is well," answered Ali.
10085-8{_}4326{_}Ou Ali arrived in the fields; one of the oxen seized him with his horns and tossed him into the air.
10085-8{_}4327{_}All the others did the same thing.
10085-8{_}4328{_}He regained the horse half dead.
10085-8{_}4329{_}Ali, who had remained at the house, asked the old woman for her daughter's hand.
10085-8{_}4330{_}"You ask me again?"
10085-8{_}4331{_}said she.
10085-8{_}4332{_}She took a club and gave it to him till he had had enough.
10085-8{_}4333{_}Ou Ali said to Ali: "You have played me a trick."
10085-8{_}4334{_}Ali answered him: "Without doubt they gave me the stick so hard that I did not hear the last blow."
10085-8{_}4335{_}"It is well, my dear friend.
10085-8{_}4336{_}Ali owes nothing to Ou Ali."
10085-8{_}4337{_}They went away.
10085-8{_}4338{_}The old woman possessed a treasure.
10085-8{_}4339{_}Ou Ali therefore said to Ali: "I will put you in a basket, for you know that we saw that treasure in a hole."
10085-8{_}4340{_}They returned to the old woman's house.
10085-8{_}4341{_}Ali goes down into the hole, takes the treasure, and puts it into the basket.
10085-8{_}4342{_}Ou Ali draws up the basket, takes it, abandons his friend, now a prisoner, and runs to hide the treasure in the forest.
10085-8{_}4343{_}Ali was in trouble, for he knew not how to get out.
10085-8{_}4344{_}What could he do?
10085-8{_}4345{_}He climbed up the sides of the hole.
10085-8{_}4346{_}When he found himself in the house, he opened the door and fled.
10085-8{_}4347{_}Arriving at the edge of the forest he began to bleat.
10085-8{_}4348{_}Ou Ali, thinking it was a ewe, ran up.
10085-8{_}4349{_}It was his friend.
10085-8{_}4350{_}"O my dear," cried Ali, "I have found you at last."
10085-8{_}4351{_}"God be praised.
10085-8{_}4352{_}Now, let us carry our treasure."
10085-8{_}4353{_}They started on the way.
10085-8{_}4354{_}Ou Ali, who had a sister, said to Ali: "Let us go to my sister's house."
10085-8{_}4355{_}They arrived at nightfall.
10085-8{_}4356{_}She received them with joy.
10085-8{_}4357{_}Her brother said to her:  "Prepare some pancakes and some eggs for us."
10085-8{_}4358{_}She prepared the pancakes and the eggs and served them with the food.
10085-8{_}4359{_}"O my sister," cried Ou Ali, "my friend does not like eggs; bring us some water."
10085-8{_}4360{_}She went to get the water.
10085-8{_}4361{_}As soon as she had gone, Ali took an egg and put it into his mouth.
10085-8{_}4362{_}When the woman returned, he made such efforts to give it up that he was all out of breath.
10085-8{_}4363{_}The repast was finished, and Ali had not eaten anything.
10085-8{_}4364{_}Ou Ali said to his sister: "O my sister, my friend is ill; bring me a skewer."
10085-8{_}4365{_}She brought him a skewer, which he put into the fire.
10085-8{_}4366{_}When the skewer was red with the heat, Ou Ali seized it and applied it to the cheek of Ali.
10085-8{_}4367{_}The latter uttered a cry, and rejected the egg.
10085-8{_}4368{_}"Truly," said the woman, "you do not like eggs."
10085-8{_}4369{_}The two friends started and arrived at a village.
10085-8{_}4370{_}"Let us go to my sister's house," said Ali to his friend.
10085-8{_}4371{_}She received them with open arms.
10085-8{_}4372{_}Ali said to her: "O my sister, prepare a good stew for us."
10085-8{_}4373{_}They placed themselves at the table at nightfall, and she served them with food.
10085-8{_}4374{_}"O my sister," cried Ali, "my friend does not like stew."
10085-8{_}4375{_}Ali ate alone.
10085-8{_}4376{_}When he was satisfied, the two friends started, without forgetting the treasure.
10085-8{_}4377{_}On the way Ali said to Ou Ali: "Give it to me to-day and I will deposit it in my house."
10085-8{_}4378{_}He took it and gave it to his wife.
10085-8{_}4379{_}"Bury me," he said to her.
10085-8{_}4380{_}"And if Ou Ali comes tell him that his old friend is dead, and receive him with tears."
10085-8{_}4381{_}Ou Ali arrived, and asked the woman in tears to see the tomb of his dead friend.
10085-8{_}4382{_}He took an ox-horn and began to dig in the earth that covered the body.
10085-8{_}4383{_}"Behind!
10085-8{_}4384{_}behind!"
10085-8{_}4385{_}cried the pretended dead man.
10085-8{_}4386{_}"Get up, there, you liar," answered Ali.
10085-8{_}4387{_}They went away together.
10085-8{_}4388{_}"Give me the treasure," asked Ou Ali; "to-day I will take it to my house."
10085-8{_}4389{_}He took it to his house, and said to his wife: "Take this treasure.
10085-8{_}4390{_}I am going to stretch myself out as if I were dead.
10085-8{_}4391{_}When Ali comes receive him weeping, and say to him: 'Your friend is dead.
10085-8{_}4392{_}He is stretched out in the bedroom.'"
10085-8{_}4393{_}Ali went and said to the woman: "Get me some boiling water, for your husband told me to wash him when he should die."
10085-8{_}4394{_}When the water was ready the woman brought it.
10085-8{_}4395{_}Ali seized the kettle and poured it on the stomach of Ou Ali, who sprang up with a bound.
10085-8{_}4396{_}Thus he got even for the trick of his friend.
10085-8{_}4397{_}The two friends divided the treasure then, and Ali went home.
10085-8{_}4398{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE INFIDEL JEW  A man went on a journey.
10085-8{_}4399{_}At the moment of departure he placed with a Jew, his friend, a jar filled with gold.
10085-8{_}4400{_}He covered the gold with butter and said to the Jew: "I trust to your care this jar of butter, as I am going on a journey."
10085-8{_}4401{_}On his return he hastened to the house of his friend.
10085-8{_}4402{_}"Give me the jar of butter that I left with you," he said.
10085-8{_}4403{_}The Jew gave it to him.
10085-8{_}4404{_}But the poor traveller found nothing but butter, for the Jew had taken the gold.
10085-8{_}4405{_}Nevertheless, he did not tell anybody of the misfortune that had happened to him.
10085-8{_}4406{_}But his countenance bore traces of a secret sorrow.
10085-8{_}4407{_}His brother perceived it, and said to him:  "What is the matter with you?"
10085-8{_}4408{_}"I intrusted a jar filled with gold to a Jew," he answered, "and he only returned a jar of butter to me.
10085-8{_}4409{_}I don't know what to do to recover my property."
10085-8{_}4410{_}His brother replied: "The thing is easy.
10085-8{_}4411{_}Prepare a feast and invite your friend the Jew."
10085-8{_}4412{_}The next day the traveller prepared a feast and invited the Jew.
10085-8{_}4413{_}During this time the brother of the traveller ran to a neighboring mountain, where he captured a monkey.
10085-8{_}4414{_}During the night he entered the house of the Jew and found a child in the cradle.
10085-8{_}4415{_}He took the child away and put the monkey in its place.
10085-8{_}4416{_}When day had come the mother perceived the monkey tied in the cradle.
10085-8{_}4417{_}She called her husband with loud cries, and said to him:  "See how God has punished us for having stolen your friend's gold.
10085-8{_}4418{_}Our child is changed into a monkey.
10085-8{_}4419{_}Give back the stolen property."
10085-8{_}4420{_}They immediately had the traveller summoned, and returned his gold to him.
10085-8{_}4421{_}The next night the child was taken back to the cradle and the monkey was set free.
10085-8{_}4422{_}As I can go no further, may God exterminate the jackal and pardon all our sins!
10085-8{_}4423{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE SHEIK'S HEAD   A man died, leaving a son.
10085-8{_}4424{_}The child spent day and night with his mother.
10085-8{_}4425{_}The sheik chanted a prayer every morning and waked him up.
10085-8{_}4426{_}The child went to find the sheik, and said:  "Ali Sheik, do not sing so loudly, you wake us up every morning--my mother and me."
10085-8{_}4427{_}But the sheik kept on singing.
10085-8{_}4428{_}The child went to the mosque armed with a club.
10085-8{_}4429{_}At the moment when the sheik bowed to pray he struck him a blow and killed him.
10085-8{_}4430{_}He ran to his mother, and said to her:  "I have killed that sheik; come, let us bury him."
10085-8{_}4431{_}They cut off his head and buried his body.
10085-8{_}4432{_}The child went to the Thadjeinath, where the men of the village were assembled.
10085-8{_}4433{_}In his absence his mother killed a sheep.
10085-8{_}4434{_}She took the head and buried it in place of the sheik's head.
10085-8{_}4435{_}The child arrived at the Thadjeinath and said to those present:  "I have killed the sheik who waked us up every morning."
10085-8{_}4436{_}"It is a lie," said they.
10085-8{_}4437{_}"Come to my mother's house and we will show you where we buried his head."
10085-8{_}4438{_}They went to the house, and the mother said to them:  "Ali Sidi, this child is mad.
10085-8{_}4439{_}It is a sheep that we have killed.
10085-8{_}4440{_}Come and see where we buried its head."
10085-8{_}4441{_}They went to the spot, dug, and found a sheep's head.
10085-8{_}4442{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE WAGTAIL AND THE JACKAL  At the time when all the animals spoke, a wagtail laid her eggs on the ground.
10085-8{_}4443{_}The little ones grew up.
10085-8{_}4444{_}A jackal and a fox came to them.
10085-8{_}4445{_}The jackal said to the fox:  "Swear to me that the wagtail owes me a pound of butter."
10085-8{_}4446{_}The fox swore to it.
10085-8{_}4447{_}The bird began to weep.
10085-8{_}4448{_}A greyhound came to her and asked her what was the matter.
10085-8{_}4449{_}She answered him:  "The fox has calumniated me."
10085-8{_}4450{_}"Well," said the hound, "put me in this sack of skin."
10085-8{_}4451{_}She put him in the sack.
10085-8{_}4452{_}"Tie up the top well," said the hound.
10085-8{_}4453{_}When the jackal returned she said to him:  "Come and measure out the butter."
10085-8{_}4454{_}The jackal advanced and unfastened the sack.
10085-8{_}4455{_}He saw the hound, who stretched out his paws and said to the fox:  "I am ill; come and measure, fox."
10085-8{_}4456{_}The fox approached.
10085-8{_}4457{_}The hound seized him.
10085-8{_}4458{_}The jackal said, "Remember your false testimony."
10085-8{_}4459{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE FLUTE-PLAYER  A servant tended the sheep of his master.
10085-8{_}4460{_}Arrived in the meadow, he played the flute.
10085-8{_}4461{_}The sheep heard him, and would not browse.
10085-8{_}4462{_}One day the master perceived that his sheep did not graze.
10085-8{_}4463{_}He followed the servant to the fields and hid himself in the bush.
10085-8{_}4464{_}The shepherd took his flute and began to play.
10085-8{_}4465{_}His master began to dance so that the bushes brought blood upon him.
10085-8{_}4466{_}He returned home.
10085-8{_}4467{_}"Who scratched you so?"
10085-8{_}4468{_}asked his wife.
10085-8{_}4469{_}"The servant played on the flute, and I began to dance."
10085-8{_}4470{_}"That is a lie," said she; "people don't dance against their will."
10085-8{_}4471{_}"Well," answered the husband, "tie me to this post and make the servant play."
10085-8{_}4472{_}She tied him to the post and the servant took the flute.
10085-8{_}4473{_}Our man began to dance.
10085-8{_}4474{_}He struck his head against a nail in the post and died.
10085-8{_}4475{_}The son of the dead man said to the servant:  "Pay me for the loss of my father."
10085-8{_}4476{_}They went before the cadi.
10085-8{_}4477{_}On the way they met a laborer, who asked them where they were going.
10085-8{_}4478{_}"Before the cadi."
10085-8{_}4479{_}"Could you tell me why?"
10085-8{_}4480{_}"This man killed my father," answered the son of the dead man.
10085-8{_}4481{_}"It was not I that killed him," answered the shepherd; "I played on the flute, he danced and died."
10085-8{_}4482{_}"That is a lie!"
10085-8{_}4483{_}cried the laborer.
10085-8{_}4484{_}"I will not dance against my will.
10085-8{_}4485{_}Take your flute and we shall see if I dance."
10085-8{_}4486{_}The shepherd took his flute.
10085-8{_}4487{_}He began to play, and the laborer started dancing with such activity that his oxen left to themselves fell into the ravine.
10085-8{_}4488{_}"Pay me for my oxen," he cried to the shepherd.
10085-8{_}4489{_}"Come before the cadi," he answered.
10085-8{_}4490{_}They presented themselves before the cadi, who received them on the second floor of the house.
10085-8{_}4491{_}They all sat down.
10085-8{_}4492{_}Then the cadi said to the servant:  "Take your flute and play before me.
10085-8{_}4493{_}I will see how you play."
10085-8{_}4494{_}The servant took his flute and all began to dance.
10085-8{_}4495{_}The cadi danced with the others, and they all fell down to the ground floor and were killed.
10085-8{_}4496{_}The servant stayed in the house of the cadi and inherited the property of all.
10085-8{_}4497{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE CHILD   A child had a thorn in his foot.
10085-8{_}4498{_}He went to an old woman and said to her:  "Take out this thorn for me."
10085-8{_}4499{_}The old woman took out the thorn and threw it away.
10085-8{_}4500{_}"Give me my thorn," and he began to cry.
10085-8{_}4501{_}"Take an egg."
10085-8{_}4502{_}He went to another old woman, "Hide me this egg."
10085-8{_}4503{_}"Put it in the hen's nest."
10085-8{_}4504{_}In the night he took his egg and ate it.
10085-8{_}4505{_}The next day he said to the old woman: "Give me my egg."
10085-8{_}4506{_}"Take the hen," she answered.
10085-8{_}4507{_}He went to another old woman, "Hide my hen for me."
10085-8{_}4508{_}"Put her on the stake to which I tie my he-goat."
10085-8{_}4509{_}At night he took away the hen.
10085-8{_}4510{_}The next morning he demanded his hen.
10085-8{_}4511{_}"Look for her where you hid her."
10085-8{_}4512{_}"Give me my hen."
10085-8{_}4513{_}"Take the he-goat."
10085-8{_}4514{_}He went to another old woman, "O old woman, hide this goat for me."
10085-8{_}4515{_}"Tie him to the sheep's crib."
10085-8{_}4516{_}During the night he took away the buck.
10085-8{_}4517{_}The next day he claimed the buck.
10085-8{_}4518{_}"Take the sheep."
10085-8{_}4519{_}He went to another old woman, "O old woman, keep my sheep for me."
10085-8{_}4520{_}"Tie him to the foot of the calf."
10085-8{_}4521{_}During the night he took away the sheep.
10085-8{_}4522{_}Next morning he demanded his sheep.
10085-8{_}4523{_}"Take the calf."
10085-8{_}4524{_}He went to another old woman, "Keep my calf for me."
10085-8{_}4525{_}"Tie him to the cow's manger."
10085-8{_}4526{_}In the night he took away the calf.
10085-8{_}4527{_}The next morning he asked for his calf.
10085-8{_}4528{_}"Take the cow."
10085-8{_}4529{_}He went to another old woman, "Keep my cow for me."
10085-8{_}4530{_}"Tie her to the foot of the old woman's bed."
10085-8{_}4531{_}In the night he took away the cow.
10085-8{_}4532{_}The next morning he demanded his cow.
10085-8{_}4533{_}"Take the old woman."
10085-8{_}4534{_}He went to another old woman and left the old dame, whom he killed during the night.
10085-8{_}4535{_}The next morning he demanded his old woman.
10085-8{_}4536{_}"There she is by the young girl."
10085-8{_}4537{_}He found her dead.
10085-8{_}4538{_}"Give me my old woman."
10085-8{_}4539{_}"Take the young girl."
10085-8{_}4540{_}He said to her: "From the thorn to the egg, from the egg to the hen, from the hen to the buck, from the buck to the sheep, from the sheep to the calf, from the calf to the cow, from the cow to the old woman, from the old woman to the young girl, and now come and marry me."
10085-8{_}4541{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE MONKEY AND THE FISHERMAN   A fisherman went one day to the sea to catch some fish.
10085-8{_}4542{_}In the evening he sold his catch, and bought a little loaf of bread, on which he made his supper.
10085-8{_}4543{_}The next day he returned to his fishing and found a chest.
10085-8{_}4544{_}He took it to his house and opened it.
10085-8{_}4545{_}Out jumped a monkey and said to him: "Bad luck to you.
10085-8{_}4546{_}I am not the only one to conquer.
10085-8{_}4547{_}You may bewail your sad lot."
10085-8{_}4548{_}"My lot is unbearable," he answered.
10085-8{_}4549{_}The next day he returned to his fishing.
10085-8{_}4550{_}The monkey climbed to the roof of the house and sat there.
10085-8{_}4551{_}A moment afterward he cut all the roses of the garden.
10085-8{_}4552{_}The daughter of the King saw him, and said to him:  "O Sidi Mahomet, what are you doing there?
10085-8{_}4553{_}Come here, I need you."
10085-8{_}4554{_}He took a rose and approached.
10085-8{_}4555{_}"Where do you live?"
10085-8{_}4556{_}asked the princess.
10085-8{_}4557{_}"With the son of the Sultan of India," answered the monkey.
10085-8{_}4558{_}"Tell him to buy me."
10085-8{_}4559{_}"I will tell him, provided he will accept."
10085-8{_}4560{_}The next day he stayed in the house and tore his face.
10085-8{_}4561{_}The princess called him again.
10085-8{_}4562{_}The monkey brought her a rose.
10085-8{_}4563{_}"Who put you in that condition?"
10085-8{_}4564{_}she cried.
10085-8{_}4565{_}"It was the son of the Sultan of India," answered the monkey.
10085-8{_}4566{_}"When I told him to buy you he gave me a blow."
10085-8{_}4567{_}The princess gave him 100 ecus, and he went away.
10085-8{_}4568{_}The next day he scratched his face worse and climbed on the house.
10085-8{_}4569{_}The daughter of the King called him:  "Sidi Mahomet!"
10085-8{_}4570{_}"Well?"
10085-8{_}4571{_}"Come here.
10085-8{_}4572{_}What did you say to him?"
10085-8{_}4573{_}"I told him to buy you, and he gave me another blow."
10085-8{_}4574{_}"Since this is so, come and find me to-morrow."
10085-8{_}4575{_}The next day the monkey took the fisherman to a shop and bought him some clothes.
10085-8{_}4576{_}He took him to the baths and made him bathe.
10085-8{_}4577{_}Then he went along the road and cried:  "Flee, flee, here is the son of the Sultan of India!"
10085-8{_}4578{_}They went into a coffee-house, and Si Mahomet ordered two coffees.
10085-8{_}4579{_}They drank their coffees, gave an ecu to the proprietor, and went out.
10085-8{_}4580{_}While going toward the palace Si Mahomet said to-the fisherman:  "Here we are at the house of your father-in-law.
10085-8{_}4581{_}When he serves us to eat, eat little.
10085-8{_}4582{_}When he offers us coffee, drink only a little of it.
10085-8{_}4583{_}You will find silken rugs stretched on the floor; keep on your sandals."
10085-8{_}4584{_}When they arrived the fisherman took off his sandals.
10085-8{_}4585{_}The King offered them something to eat; the fisherman ate a great deal.
10085-8{_}4586{_}He offered them some coffee, and the fisherman did not leave a drop of it.
10085-8{_}4587{_}They went out.
10085-8{_}4588{_}When they were outside the palace Si Mahomet said to the fisherman:  "Jew of a fisherman, you are lucky that I do not scratch your face."
10085-8{_}4589{_}They returned to their house.
10085-8{_}4590{_}Si Mahomet climbed upon the roof.
10085-8{_}4591{_}The daughter of the King perceived him, and said:  "Come here."
10085-8{_}4592{_}The monkey approached.
10085-8{_}4593{_}"Truly you have lied.
10085-8{_}4594{_}Why did you tell me that the son of the Sultan of India was a distinguished person?"
10085-8{_}4595{_}"Is he a worthless fellow?"
10085-8{_}4596{_}"We furnished the room with silken rugs, he took off his sandals.
10085-8{_}4597{_}We gave him food, and he ate like a servant.
10085-8{_}4598{_}We offered him some coffee, and he licked his fingers."
10085-8{_}4599{_}The monkey answered: "We had just come out of the coffeehouse.
10085-8{_}4600{_}He had taken too much wine and was drunken, and not master of himself.
10085-8{_}4601{_}That is why he ate so much."
10085-8{_}4602{_}"Well," replied the princess, "come to the palace again tomorrow, but do not take him to the coffee-house first."
10085-8{_}4603{_}The next day they set out.
10085-8{_}4604{_}On the way the monkey said to the fisherman: "Jew of a fisherman, if to-day you take off your sandals or eat too much or drink all your coffee, look out for yourself.
10085-8{_}4605{_}Drink a little only, or I will scratch your eyes out."
10085-8{_}4606{_}They arrived at the palace.
10085-8{_}4607{_}The fisherman walked on the silken rugs with his sandals.
10085-8{_}4608{_}They gave him something to eat, and he ate little.
10085-8{_}4609{_}They brought him some coffee, and he hardly tasted it.
10085-8{_}4610{_}The King gave him his daughter.
10085-8{_}4611{_}Si Mahomet said to the King:  "The son of the Sultan of India has quarrelled with his father, so he only brought one chest of silver."
10085-8{_}4612{_}In the evening the monkey and the fisherman went out for a walk.
10085-8{_}4613{_}The fisherman said to Si Mahomet:  "Is it here that we are going to find the son of the Sultan of India?"
10085-8{_}4614{_}"I can show him to you easily," answered the monkey.
10085-8{_}4615{_}"Tomorrow I will find you seated.
10085-8{_}4616{_}I will approach, weeping, with a paper in my hands; I will give you the paper, and you must read it and burst into tears.
10085-8{_}4617{_}Your father-in-law will ask you why you weep so.
10085-8{_}4618{_}Answer him: 'My father is dead.
10085-8{_}4619{_}Here is the letter I have just received.
10085-8{_}4620{_}If you have finally determined to give me your daughter, I will take her away and we will go to pay the last duties to my father.'"
10085-8{_}4621{_}"Take her," said the King.
10085-8{_}4622{_}He gave him an escort of horsemen and soldiers.
10085-8{_}4623{_}Arriving at the place, Si Mahomet said to the soldiers:  "You may return to the palace, for our country is far from here."
10085-8{_}4624{_}The escort went back to the palace, and the travellers continued on their journey.
10085-8{_}4625{_}Soon Si Mahomet said to the fisherman: "Stay here till I go and look at the country of your father."
10085-8{_}4626{_}He started, and arrived at the gates of a city he found closed he mounted upon the ramparts.
10085-8{_}4627{_}An ogress perceived him, "I salute you, Si Mahomet."
10085-8{_}4628{_}"May God curse you, sorceress!
10085-8{_}4629{_}Come, I am going to your house."
10085-8{_}4630{_}"What do you want of me, Si Mahomet?"
10085-8{_}4631{_}"They are seeking to kill you."
10085-8{_}4632{_}"Where can I hide?"
10085-8{_}4633{_}He put her in the powder-house of the city, shut the door on her, and set the powder on fire.
10085-8{_}4634{_}The ogress died.
10085-8{_}4635{_}He came back to the fisherman.
10085-8{_}4636{_}"Forward," he said.
10085-8{_}4637{_}They entered the city and established themselves there.
10085-8{_}4638{_}One day Si Mahomet fell ill and died The two spouses put him in a coffin lined with silk and buried him.
10085-8{_}4639{_}My story is told.
10085-8{_}4640{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE TWO FRIENDS  Sidi El-Marouf and Sidi Abd-el-Tadu were travelling in company.
10085-8{_}4641{_}Toward evening they separated to find a resting-place.
10085-8{_}4642{_}Sidi Abd-el-Tadu said to his friend:  "Let us say a prayer, that God may preserve us from the evil which we have never committed."
10085-8{_}4643{_}Sidi El-Marouf answered, "Yes, may God preserve us from the evil that we have not done!"
10085-8{_}4644{_}They went toward the houses, each his own way.
10085-8{_}4645{_}Sidi El-Marouf presented himself at a door.
10085-8{_}4646{_}"Can you entertain a traveller?"
10085-8{_}4647{_}"You are welcome," said a woman to him.
10085-8{_}4648{_}"Enter, you may remain for the night."
10085-8{_}4649{_}Night came.
10085-8{_}4650{_}He took his supper.
10085-8{_}4651{_}The woman spread a mat on the floor and he went to sleep.
10085-8{_}4652{_}The woman and her husband slept also.
10085-8{_}4653{_}When all was quiet, the woman got up, took a knife, and killed her husband.
10085-8{_}4654{_}The next day at dawn she began to cry:  "He has killed my husband!"
10085-8{_}4655{_}The whole village ran up to the house and seized the stranger.
10085-8{_}4656{_}They bound him, and everyone brought wood to burn the guilty man.
10085-8{_}4657{_}Sidi Abd-el-Tadu came also, and saw his friend in tears.
10085-8{_}4658{_}"What have you done?"
10085-8{_}4659{_}he asked.
10085-8{_}4660{_}"I have done no evil," answered Sidi El-Marouf.
10085-8{_}4661{_}"Did I not tell you yesterday," said Sidi Abd-el-Tadu, "that we would say the prayer that God should preserve us from the evil we had never committed?
10085-8{_}4662{_}And now you will be burned for a crime of which you are innocent!"
10085-8{_}4663{_}Sidi El-Marouf answered him, "Bring the woman here."
10085-8{_}4664{_}"Did he really kill your husband?"
10085-8{_}4665{_}asked Sidi Abd-el-Tadu.
10085-8{_}4666{_}"He killed him," she replied.
10085-8{_}4667{_}There was a bird on a tree nearby.
10085-8{_}4668{_}Sidi Abd-el-Tadu asked the bird.
10085-8{_}4669{_}The bird answered:  "It was the woman who killed her husband.
10085-8{_}4670{_}Feel in her hair and you will find the knife she used."
10085-8{_}4671{_}They searched her hair and found the knife still covered with blood, which gave evidence of the crime.
10085-8{_}4672{_}The truth was known and innocence was defended.
10085-8{_}4673{_}God avenged the injustice.
10085-8{_}4674{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE ROBBER AND THE TWO PILGRIMS   Two robbers spent their time in robbing.
10085-8{_}4675{_}One of them got married, and the other continued his trade.
10085-8{_}4676{_}They were a long time without seeing each other.
10085-8{_}4677{_}Finally the one who was not married went to visit his friend, and said to him:  "If your wife has a daughter, you must give her to me."
10085-8{_}4678{_}"I will give her to you seven days after her birth."
10085-8{_}4679{_}The daughter was born, and the robber took her to bring up in the country.
10085-8{_}4680{_}He built a house, bought flocks, and tended them himself.
10085-8{_}4681{_}One day some pilgrims came to the house.
10085-8{_}4682{_}He killed a cow for them and entertained them.
10085-8{_}4683{_}The next day he accompanied them on their pilgrimage.
10085-8{_}4684{_}The pilgrims said to him:  "If you come with us, two birds will remain with your wife."
10085-8{_}4685{_}The woman stayed in the country.
10085-8{_}4686{_}One day the son of the Sultan came that way to hunt.
10085-8{_}4687{_}One of the birds saw him and said to the woman, "Don't open the door."
10085-8{_}4688{_}The prince heard the bird speak, and returned to the palace without saying a word.
10085-8{_}4689{_}An old woman was called to cast spells over him, and said to the King:  "He could not see a woman he has never seen."
10085-8{_}4690{_}The prince spoke and said to her: "If you will come with me, I will bring her here."
10085-8{_}4691{_}They arrived.
10085-8{_}4692{_}The old dame called the young woman, "Come out, that we may see you."
10085-8{_}4693{_}She said to the bird, "I am going to open the door."
10085-8{_}4694{_}The bird answered: "If you open the door you will meet the same fate as Si El-Ahcen.
10085-8{_}4695{_}He was reading with many others in the mosque.
10085-8{_}4696{_}One day he found an amulet.
10085-8{_}4697{_}His betrothed went no longer to school, and as she was old enough he married her.
10085-8{_}4698{_}Some days after he said to his father, 'Watch over my wife.'
10085-8{_}4699{_}'Fear nothing,' answered the father.
10085-8{_}4700{_}"He started, and came back.
10085-8{_}4701{_}'Watch over my wife,' he said to his father again.
10085-8{_}4702{_}'Fear nothing,' repeated his father.
10085-8{_}4703{_}The latter went to the market.
10085-8{_}4704{_}On his return he said to his daughter-in-law, 'There were very beautiful women in the market,' 'I surpass them all in beauty,' said the woman; 'take me to the market.'
10085-8{_}4705{_}"A man offered 1,000 francs for her.
10085-8{_}4706{_}The father-in-law refused, and said to her: 'Sit down on the mat.
10085-8{_}4707{_}The one that covers you with silver may have you,' A man advanced.
10085-8{_}4708{_}'If you want to marry her,' said her father-in-law, 'cover her with silver, and she will be your wife.'
10085-8{_}4709{_}"Soon Si El-Ahcen returned from his journey and asked if his wife were still living.
10085-8{_}4710{_}'Your wife is dead,' said his father; 'she fell from her mule,' Si El-Ahcen threw himself on the ground.
10085-8{_}4711{_}They tried to lift him up.
10085-8{_}4712{_}It was useless trouble.
10085-8{_}4713{_}He remained stretched on the earth.
10085-8{_}4714{_}"One day a merchant came to the village and said to him, 'The Sultan married your wife,' She had said to the merchant, 'The day that you leave I will give you a message,' She wrote a letter to her husband, and promised the bearer a flock of sheep if he would deliver it.
10085-8{_}4715{_}"Si El-Ahcen received the letter, read it, was cured, ran to the house, and said to his father: 'My wife has married again in my absence; she is not dead.
10085-8{_}4716{_}I brought home much money.
10085-8{_}4717{_}I will take it again.'
10085-8{_}4718{_}"He took his money and went to the city where his wife lived.
10085-8{_}4719{_}He stopped at the gates.
10085-8{_}4720{_}To the first passer-by he gave five francs, to the second five more.
10085-8{_}4721{_}"'What do you want, O stranger?'
10085-8{_}4722{_}they asked.
10085-8{_}4723{_}'If you want to see the Sultan we will take you to him,' They presented him to the Sultan.
10085-8{_}4724{_}"'Render justice to this man,' 'What does he want?'
10085-8{_}4725{_}'My lord,' answered Sidi El-Ahcen, 'the woman you married is my wife,' 'Kill him!'
10085-8{_}4726{_}cried the Sultan.
10085-8{_}4727{_}'No,' said the witnesses, 'let him have justice,'  "'Let him tell me if she carries an object,' Si El-Ahcen answered: 'This woman was betrothed to me before her birth.
10085-8{_}4728{_}An amulet is hidden in her hair,' He took away his wife, returned to the village, and gave a feast.
10085-8{_}4729{_}"If you open the door," continued the bird, "you will have the same fate as Fatima-ou-Lmelh.
10085-8{_}4730{_}Hamed-ou-Lmelh married her.
10085-8{_}4731{_}Fatima said to her father-in-law, 'Take me to my uncle's house,' Arriving there she married another husband.
10085-8{_}4732{_}Hamed-ou-Lmelh was told of this, and ran to find her.
10085-8{_}4733{_}At the moment he arrived he found the wedding over and the bride about to depart for the house of her new husband.
10085-8{_}4734{_}Then Hamed burst into the room and cast himself out of the window.
10085-8{_}4735{_}Fatima did the same, and they were both killed.
10085-8{_}4736{_}"The intended father-in-law and his family returned to their house, and were asked the cause of the misfortune.
10085-8{_}4737{_}'The woman was the cause,' they answered.
10085-8{_}4738{_}"Nevertheless, the father of Hamed-ou-Lmelh went to the parents of Fatima and said: 'Pay us for the loss of our son.
10085-8{_}4739{_}Pay us for the loss of Fatima.'
10085-8{_}4740{_}"They could not agree, and went before the justice.
10085-8{_}4741{_}Passing by the village where the two spouses had died they met an old man, and said, 'Settle our dispute,' 'I cannot,' answered the old man.
10085-8{_}4742{_}Farther on they met a sheep, which was butting a rock.
10085-8{_}4743{_}'Settle our dispute,' they said to the sheep.
10085-8{_}4744{_}'I cannot,' answered the sheep.
10085-8{_}4745{_}Farther on they met a serpent.
10085-8{_}4746{_}'Settle our dispute,' they said to him.
10085-8{_}4747{_}'I cannot,' answered the serpent.
10085-8{_}4748{_}They met a river.
10085-8{_}4749{_}'Settle our dispute,' they said to it.
10085-8{_}4750{_}'I cannot,' answered the river.
10085-8{_}4751{_}They met a jackal.
10085-8{_}4752{_}'Settle our dispute,' they said to him.
10085-8{_}4753{_}'Go to the village where your children died,' answered the jackal.
10085-8{_}4754{_}They went back to the village, and applied to the Sultan, who had them all killed."
10085-8{_}4755{_}The bird stopped speaking, the pilgrims returned.
10085-8{_}4756{_}The old woman saw them and fled.
10085-8{_}4757{_}The robber prepared a feast for the pilgrims.
10085-8{_}4758{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE LITTLE CHILD  "Come, little child, eat your dinner."
10085-8{_}4759{_}"I won't eat it."
10085-8{_}4760{_}"Come, stick, beat the child."
10085-8{_}4761{_}"I won't beat him."
10085-8{_}4762{_}"Come, fire, burn the stick."
10085-8{_}4763{_}"I won't burn it."
10085-8{_}4764{_}"Come, water, quench the fire."
10085-8{_}4765{_}"I won't quench it."
10085-8{_}4766{_}"Come, ox, drink the water."
10085-8{_}4767{_}"I won't drink it."
10085-8{_}4768{_}"Come, knife, kill the ox."
10085-8{_}4769{_}"I won't kill him."
10085-8{_}4770{_}"Come, blacksmith, break the knife."
10085-8{_}4771{_}"I won't break it."
10085-8{_}4772{_}"Come, strap, bind the blacksmith."
10085-8{_}4773{_}"I won't bind him."
10085-8{_}4774{_}"Come, rat, gnaw the strap."
10085-8{_}4775{_}"I won't gnaw it."
10085-8{_}4776{_}"Come, cat, eat the rat."
10085-8{_}4777{_}"Bring it here."
10085-8{_}4778{_}"Why eat me?"
10085-8{_}4779{_}said the rat; "bring the strap and I'll gnaw it."
10085-8{_}4780{_}"Why gnaw me?"
10085-8{_}4781{_}said the strap; "bring the blacksmith and I'll bind him."
10085-8{_}4782{_}"Why bind me?"
10085-8{_}4783{_}said the blacksmith; "bring the knife and I'll break it."
10085-8{_}4784{_}"Why break me?"
10085-8{_}4785{_}said the knife; "bring the ox and I'll kill him."
10085-8{_}4786{_}"Why kill me?"
10085-8{_}4787{_}said the ox; "bring the water and I'll drink it."
10085-8{_}4788{_}"Why drink me?"
10085-8{_}4789{_}said the water; "bring the fire and I'll quench it."
10085-8{_}4790{_}"Why quench me?"
10085-8{_}4791{_}said the fire; "bring the stick and I'll burn it."
10085-8{_}4792{_}"Why burn me?"
10085-8{_}4793{_}said the stick; "bring the child and I'll strike him."
10085-8{_}4794{_}"Why strike me?"
10085-8{_}4795{_}said the child; "bring me my dinner and I'll eat it."
10085-8{_}4796{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE WREN  A wren had built its nest on the side of a road.
10085-8{_}4797{_}When the eggs were hatched, a camel passed that way.
10085-8{_}4798{_}The little wrens saw it, and said to their father when he returned from the fields:  "O papa, a gigantic animal passed by."
10085-8{_}4799{_}The wren stretched out his foot.
10085-8{_}4800{_}"As big as this, my children?"
10085-8{_}4801{_}"O papa, much bigger."
10085-8{_}4802{_}He stretched out his foot and his wing.
10085-8{_}4803{_}"As big as this?"
10085-8{_}4804{_}"O papa, much bigger."
10085-8{_}4805{_}Finally he stretched out fully his feet and legs.
10085-8{_}4806{_}"As big as this, then?"
10085-8{_}4807{_}"Much bigger."
10085-8{_}4808{_}"That is a lie; there is no animal bigger than I am."
10085-8{_}4809{_}"Well, wait," said the little ones, "and you will see."
10085-8{_}4810{_}The camel came back while browsing the grass of the roadside.
10085-8{_}4811{_}The wren stretched himself out near the nest.
10085-8{_}4812{_}The camel seized the bird, which passed through its teeth safe and sound.
10085-8{_}4813{_}"Truly," he said to them, "the camel is a gigantic animal, but I am not ashamed of myself."
10085-8{_}4814{_}On the earth it generally happens that the vain are as if they did not exist.
10085-8{_}4815{_}But sooner or later a rock falls and crushes them.
10085-8{_}4816{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE MULE, THE JACKAL, AND THE LION  The mule, the jackal, and the lion went in company.
10085-8{_}4817{_}"We will eat the one whose race is bad," they said to each other.
10085-8{_}4818{_}"Lion, who is your father?"
10085-8{_}4819{_}"My father is a lion and my mother is a lioness."
10085-8{_}4820{_}"And you, jackal, what is your father?"
10085-8{_}4821{_}"My father is a jackal and my mother, too."
10085-8{_}4822{_}"And you, mule, what is your father?"
10085-8{_}4823{_}"My father is an ass, and my mother is a mare."
10085-8{_}4824{_}"Your race is bad; we will eat you."
10085-8{_}4825{_}He answered them: "I will consult an old man.
10085-8{_}4826{_}If he says that my race is bad, you may devour me."
10085-8{_}4827{_}He went to a farrier, and said to him, "Shoe my hind feet, and make the nails stick out well."
10085-8{_}4828{_}He went back home.
10085-8{_}4829{_}He called the camel and showed him his feet, saying: "See what is written on this tablet."
10085-8{_}4830{_}"The writing is difficult to decipher," answered the camel.
10085-8{_}4831{_}"I do not understand it, for I only know three words--_outini, ouzatini, ouazakin_."
10085-8{_}4832{_}He called a lion, and said to him: "I do not understand these letters; I only know three words--_outini, ouzatini, ouazakin_"  "Show it to me," said the lion.
10085-8{_}4833{_}He approached.
10085-8{_}4834{_}The mule struck him between the eyes and stretched him out stiff.
10085-8{_}4835{_}He who goes with a knave is betrayed by him.
10085-8{_}4836{_}*       *       *       *       *   THADHELLALA   A woman had seven daughters and no son.
10085-8{_}4837{_}She went to the city, and there saw a rich shop.
10085-8{_}4838{_}A little farther on she perceived at the door of a house a young girl of great beauty.
10085-8{_}4839{_}She called her parents, and said:  "I have my son to marry; let me have your daughter for him."
10085-8{_}4840{_}They let her take the girl away.
10085-8{_}4841{_}She came back to the shop and said to the man in charge of it:  "I will gladly give you my daughter; but go first and consult your father."
10085-8{_}4842{_}The young man left a servant in his place and departed.
10085-8{_}4843{_}Thadhellala (that was her name) sent the servant to buy some bread in another part of the city.
10085-8{_}4844{_}Along came a caravan of mules.
10085-8{_}4845{_}Thadhellala packed all the contents of the shop on their backs and said to the muleteer:  "I will go on ahead; my son will come in a moment.
10085-8{_}4846{_}Wait for him--he will pay you."
10085-8{_}4847{_}She went off with the mules and the treasures which she had packed upon them.
10085-8{_}4848{_}The servant came back soon.
10085-8{_}4849{_}"Where is your mother?"
10085-8{_}4850{_}cried the muleteer; "hurry and, pay me."
10085-8{_}4851{_}"You tell me where she is and I will make her give me back what she has stolen."
10085-8{_}4852{_}And they went before the justice.
10085-8{_}4853{_}Thadhellala pursued her way, and met seven young students.
10085-8{_}4854{_}She said to one of them, "A hundred francs and I will marry you."
10085-8{_}4855{_}The student gave them to her.
10085-8{_}4856{_}She made the same offer to the others, and each one took her word.
10085-8{_}4857{_}Arriving at a fork in the road, the first one said, "I will take you," the second one said, "I will take you," and so on to the last.
10085-8{_}4858{_}Thadhellala answered: "You shall have a race as far as that ridge over there, and the one that gets there first shall marry me."
10085-8{_}4859{_}The young men started.
10085-8{_}4860{_}Just then a horseman came passing by.
10085-8{_}4861{_}"Lend me your horse," she said to him.
10085-8{_}4862{_}The horseman jumped off.
10085-8{_}4863{_}Thadhellala mounted the horse and said:  "You see that ridge?
10085-8{_}4864{_}I will rejoin you there."
10085-8{_}4865{_}The scholars perceived the man.
10085-8{_}4866{_}"Have you not seen a woman?"
10085-8{_}4867{_}they asked him.
10085-8{_}4868{_}"She has stolen 700 francs from us."
10085-8{_}4869{_}"Haven't you others seen her?
10085-8{_}4870{_}She has stolen my horse?"
10085-8{_}4871{_}They went to complain to the Sultan, who gave the command to arrest Thadhellala.
10085-8{_}4872{_}A man promised to seize her.
10085-8{_}4873{_}He secured a comrade, and they both pursued Thadhellala, who had taken flight.
10085-8{_}4874{_}Nearly overtaken by the man, she met a negro who pulled teeth, and said to him:  "You see my son coming down there; pull out his teeth."
10085-8{_}4875{_}When the other passed the negro pulled out his teeth.
10085-8{_}4876{_}The poor toothless one seized the negro and led him before the Sultan to have him punished.
10085-8{_}4877{_}The negro said to the Sultan: "It was his mother that told me to pull them out for him."
10085-8{_}4878{_}"Sidi," said the accuser, "I was pursuing Thadhellala."
10085-8{_}4879{_}The Sultan then sent soldiers in pursuit of the woman, who seized her and hung her up at the gates of the city.
10085-8{_}4880{_}Seeing herself arrested, she sent a messenger to her relatives.
10085-8{_}4881{_}Then there came by a man who led a mule.
10085-8{_}4882{_}Seeing her he said, "How has this woman deserved to be hanged in this way?"
10085-8{_}4883{_}"Take pity on me," said Thadhellala; "give me your mule and I will show you a treasure."
10085-8{_}4884{_}She sent him to a certain place where the pretended treasure was supposed to be hidden.
10085-8{_}4885{_}At this the brother-in-law of Thadhellala had arrived.
10085-8{_}4886{_}"Take away this mule," she said to him.
10085-8{_}4887{_}The searcher for treasures dug in the earth at many places and found nothing.
10085-8{_}4888{_}He came back to Thadhellala and demanded his mule.
10085-8{_}4889{_}She began to weep and cry.
10085-8{_}4890{_}The sentinel ran up, and Thadhellala brought complaint against this man.
10085-8{_}4891{_}She was released, and he was hanged in her place.
10085-8{_}4892{_}She fled to a far city, of which the Sultan had just then died.
10085-8{_}4893{_}Now, according to the custom of that country, they took as king the person who happened to be at the gates of the city when the King died.
10085-8{_}4894{_}Fate took Thadhellala there at the right time.
10085-8{_}4895{_}They conducted her to the palace, and she was proclaimed Queen.
10085-8{_}4896{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE GOOD MAN AND THE BAD ONE   Two men, one good and the other bad, started out together to do business, and took provisions with them.
10085-8{_}4897{_}Soon the bad one said to the good one: "I am hungry; give me some of your food."
10085-8{_}4898{_}He gave him some, and they both ate.
10085-8{_}4899{_}They went on again till they were hungry.
10085-8{_}4900{_}"Give me some of your food," said the bad one.
10085-8{_}4901{_}He gave him some of it, and they ate.
10085-8{_}4902{_}They went on until they were hungry.
10085-8{_}4903{_}"Give me some of your food," said the bad one.
10085-8{_}4904{_}He gave him some, and they ate.
10085-8{_}4905{_}They went on until they were hungry.
10085-8{_}4906{_}The good man said to his companion: "Give me some of your food."
10085-8{_}4907{_}"Oh, no, my dear," said the bad one.
10085-8{_}4908{_}"I beg you to give me some of your food," said the good one.
10085-8{_}4909{_}"Let me pluck out one of your eyes," answered the bad one.
10085-8{_}4910{_}He consented.
10085-8{_}4911{_}The bad one took his pincers and took out one of his eyes.
10085-8{_}4912{_}They went on until they came to a certain place.
10085-8{_}4913{_}Hunger pressed them.
10085-8{_}4914{_}"Give me some of your food," said the good man.
10085-8{_}4915{_}"Let me pluck out your other eye," answered his companion.
10085-8{_}4916{_}"O my dear," replied the good man, "leave it to me, I beg of you."
10085-8{_}4917{_}"No!"
10085-8{_}4918{_}responded the bad one; "no eye, no food."
10085-8{_}4919{_}But finally he said, "Pluck it out."
10085-8{_}4920{_}They proceeded until they came to a certain place.
10085-8{_}4921{_}When hunger pressed them anew the bad one abandoned his companion.
10085-8{_}4922{_}A bird came passing by, and said to him: "Take a leaf of this tree and apply it to your eyes."
10085-8{_}4923{_}He took a leaf of the tree, applied it to his eyes, and was healed.
10085-8{_}4924{_}He arose, continued on his way, and arrived at a city where he found the one who had plucked out his eyes.
10085-8{_}4925{_}"Who cured you?"
10085-8{_}4926{_}"A bird passed near me," said the good man.
10085-8{_}4927{_}"He said to me, 'Take a leaf of this tree.'
10085-8{_}4928{_}I took it, applied it to my eyes, and was cured."
10085-8{_}4929{_}The good man found the King of the city blind.
10085-8{_}4930{_}"Give me back my sight and I will give you my daughter."
10085-8{_}4931{_}He restored his sight to him, and the King gave him his daughter.
10085-8{_}4932{_}The good man took his wife to his house.
10085-8{_}4933{_}Every morning he went to present his respects to the King, and kissed his head.
10085-8{_}4934{_}One day he fell ill.
10085-8{_}4935{_}He met the bad one, who said to him:  "Eat an onion and you will be cured; but when you kiss the King's head, turn your head aside or the King will notice your breath and will kill you."
10085-8{_}4936{_}After these words he ran to the King and said: "O King, your son-in-law disdains you."
10085-8{_}4937{_}"O my dear," answered the King, "my son-in-law does not disdain me."
10085-8{_}4938{_}"Watch him," answered the bad one; "when he comes to kiss your head he will turn away from you."
10085-8{_}4939{_}The King remarked that his son-in-law did turn away on kissing his head.
10085-8{_}4940{_}"Wait a moment," he said to him.
10085-8{_}4941{_}Immediately he wrote a letter to the Sultan, and gave it to his son-in-law, commanding him to carry it to the Sultan.
10085-8{_}4942{_}Going out of the house he met the bad one, who wanted to carry the letter himself.
10085-8{_}4943{_}The good man gave it to him.
10085-8{_}4944{_}The Sultan read the letter, and had the bad one's head cut off.
10085-8{_}4945{_}The good man returned to the King.
10085-8{_}4946{_}"What did he say?"
10085-8{_}4947{_}asked the King.
10085-8{_}4948{_}"Ah, Sidi, I met a man who wanted to carry the letter.
10085-8{_}4949{_}I intrusted it to him and he took it to the Sultan, who condemned him to death in the city."
10085-8{_}4950{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE CROW AND THE CHILD   A man had two wives.
10085-8{_}4951{_}He was a rich merchant.
10085-8{_}4952{_}One of them had a son whose forehead was curved with a forelock.
10085-8{_}4953{_}Her husband said to her:  "Don't work any more, but only take care of the child.
10085-8{_}4954{_}The other wife will do all the work."
10085-8{_}4955{_}One day he went to market.
10085-8{_}4956{_}The childless wife said to the other, "Go, get some water."
10085-8{_}4957{_}"No," she answered, "our husband does not want me to work."
10085-8{_}4958{_}"Go, get some water, I tell you."
10085-8{_}4959{_}And the woman went to the fountain.
10085-8{_}4960{_}On the way she met a crow half dead with fatigue.
10085-8{_}4961{_}A merchant who was passing took it up and carried it away.
10085-8{_}4962{_}He arrived before the house of the woman who had gone to the fountain, and there found the second woman.
10085-8{_}4963{_}"Give something to this crow," demanded the merchant.
10085-8{_}4964{_}"Give it to me," she answered, "and I will make you rich."
10085-8{_}4965{_}"What will you give me?"
10085-8{_}4966{_}asked the merchant.
10085-8{_}4967{_}"A child," replied the woman.
10085-8{_}4968{_}The merchant refused, and said to her, "Where did you steal it?"
10085-8{_}4969{_}"From whom did I steal it?"
10085-8{_}4970{_}she cried.
10085-8{_}4971{_}"It is my own son."
10085-8{_}4972{_}"Bring him."
10085-8{_}4973{_}She brought the child to him, and the merchant left her the crow and took the boy to his home and soon became very, rich.
10085-8{_}4974{_}The mother came back from the fountain.
10085-8{_}4975{_}The other woman said:  "Where is your son?
10085-8{_}4976{_}Listen, he is crying, that son of yours."
10085-8{_}4977{_}"He is not crying," she answered.
10085-8{_}4978{_}"You don't know how to amuse him.
10085-8{_}4979{_}I'll go and take him."
10085-8{_}4980{_}"Leave him alone," said the mother.
10085-8{_}4981{_}"He is asleep."
10085-8{_}4982{_}They ground some wheat, and the child did not appear to wake up.
10085-8{_}4983{_}At this the husband returned from the market and said to the mother, "Why don't you busy yourself looking after your son?"
10085-8{_}4984{_}Then she arose to take him, and found a crow in the cradle.
10085-8{_}4985{_}The other woman cried:  "This is the mother of a crow!
10085-8{_}4986{_}Take it into the other house; sprinkle it with hot water."
10085-8{_}4987{_}She went to the other house and poured hot water on the crow.
10085-8{_}4988{_}Meanwhile, the child called the merchant his father and the merchant's wife his mother.
10085-8{_}4989{_}One day the merchant set off on a journey.
10085-8{_}4990{_}His mother brought some food to him in the room where he was confined.
10085-8{_}4991{_}"My son," she said, "will you promise not to betray me?"
10085-8{_}4992{_}"You are my mother," answered the child; "I will not betray you."
10085-8{_}4993{_}"Only promise me."
10085-8{_}4994{_}"I promise not to betray you."
10085-8{_}4995{_}"Well, know that I am not your mother and my husband is not your father."
10085-8{_}4996{_}The merchant came home from his journey and took the child some food, but he would not eat it.
10085-8{_}4997{_}"Why won't you eat?"
10085-8{_}4998{_}asked the merchant.
10085-8{_}4999{_}"Could your mother have been here?"
10085-8{_}5000{_}"No," answered the child, "she has not been here."
10085-8{_}5001{_}The merchant went to his wife and said to her, "Could you have gone up to the child's chamber?"
10085-8{_}5002{_}The woman answered, "I did not go up to the room."
10085-8{_}5003{_}The merchant carried food to the child, who said: "For the love of God, I adjure you to tell me if you are my father and if your wife is my mother."
10085-8{_}5004{_}The merchant answered: "My son, I am not your father and my wife is not your mother."
10085-8{_}5005{_}The child said to her, "Prepare us some food."
10085-8{_}5006{_}When she had prepared the food the child mounted a horse and the merchant a mule.
10085-8{_}5007{_}They proceeded a long way, and arrived at the village of which the real father of the child was the chief.
10085-8{_}5008{_}They entered his house.
10085-8{_}5009{_}They gave food to the child, and said, "Eat."
10085-8{_}5010{_}"I will not eat until the other woman comes up here."
10085-8{_}5011{_}"Eat.
10085-8{_}5012{_}She is a bad woman."
10085-8{_}5013{_}"No, let her come up."
10085-8{_}5014{_}They called her.
10085-8{_}5015{_}The merchant ran to the child.
10085-8{_}5016{_}"Why do you act thus toward her?"
10085-8{_}5017{_}"Oh!"
10085-8{_}5018{_}cried those present, "she had a child that was changed into a crow."
10085-8{_}5019{_}"No doubt," said the merchant; "but the child had a mark."
10085-8{_}5020{_}"Yes, he had one."
10085-8{_}5021{_}"Well, if we find it, we shall recognize the child.
10085-8{_}5022{_}Put out the lamp."
10085-8{_}5023{_}They put it out.
10085-8{_}5024{_}The child threw off its hood.
10085-8{_}5025{_}They lighted the lamp again.
10085-8{_}5026{_}"Rejoice," cried the child, "I am your son!"
10085-8{_}5027{_}*       *       *       *       *   H'AB SLIMAN   A man had a boy and a girl.
10085-8{_}5028{_}Their mother died and he took another wife.
10085-8{_}5029{_}The little boy stayed at school until evening.
10085-8{_}5030{_}The school-master asked them:  "What do your sisters do?"
10085-8{_}5031{_}One answered, "She makes bread."
10085-8{_}5032{_}A second, "She goes to fetch water."
10085-8{_}5033{_}A third, "She prepares the _couscous_."
10085-8{_}5034{_}When he questioned H'ab Sliman, the child played deaf, the master struck him.
10085-8{_}5035{_}One day his sister said to him: "What is the matter, O my brother?
10085-8{_}5036{_}You seem to be sad."
10085-8{_}5037{_}"Our schoolmaster punishes us," answered the child.
10085-8{_}5038{_}"And why does he punish you?"
10085-8{_}5039{_}inquired the young girl.
10085-8{_}5040{_}The child replied: "After we have studied until evening he asks each of us what our sisters do.
10085-8{_}5041{_}They answer him: she kneads bread, she goes to get water.
10085-8{_}5042{_}But when he questions me I have nothing to say, and he beats me."
10085-8{_}5043{_}"Is it nothing but for that?"
10085-8{_}5044{_}"That is all."
10085-8{_}5045{_}"Well," added the young girl, "the next time he asks you, answer him: 'This is what my sister does: When she laughs the sun shines; when she weeps it rains; when she combs her hair, legs of mutton fall; when she goes from one place to another, roses drop.'"
10085-8{_}5046{_}The child gave that answer.
10085-8{_}5047{_}"Truly," said the schoolmaster, "that is a rich match."
10085-8{_}5048{_}A few days after he bought her, and they made preparations for her departure for the house of her husband.
10085-8{_}5049{_}The stepmother of the young girl made her a little loaf of salt bread.
10085-8{_}5050{_}She ate it and asked some drink from her sister, the daughter of her stepmother.
10085-8{_}5051{_}"Let me pluck out one of your eyes," said the sister.
10085-8{_}5052{_}"Pluck it out," said the promised bride, "for our people are already on the way."
10085-8{_}5053{_}The stepmother gave her to drink and plucked out one of her eyes.
10085-8{_}5054{_}"A little more," she said.
10085-8{_}5055{_}"Let me take out your other eye," answered the cruel woman.
10085-8{_}5056{_}The young girl drank and let her pluck out the other eye.
10085-8{_}5057{_}Scarcely had she left the house than the stepmother thrust her out on the road.
10085-8{_}5058{_}She dressed her own daughter and put her in the place of the blind one.
10085-8{_}5059{_}They arrive.
10085-8{_}5060{_}"Comb yourself," they told her, and there fell dust.
10085-8{_}5061{_}"Walk," and nothing happened.
10085-8{_}5062{_}"Laugh," and her front teeth fell out.
10085-8{_}5063{_}All cried, "Hang H'ab Sliman!"
10085-8{_}5064{_}Meanwhile some crows came flying near the young blind girl, and one said to her: "Some merchants are on the point of passing this way.
10085-8{_}5065{_}Ask them for a little wool, and I will restore your sight."
10085-8{_}5066{_}The merchants came up and the blind girl asked them for a little wool, and each one of them threw her a bit.
10085-8{_}5067{_}The crow descended near her and restored her sight.
10085-8{_}5068{_}"Into what shall we change you?"
10085-8{_}5069{_}they asked.
10085-8{_}5070{_}"Change me into a pigeon," she answered.
10085-8{_}5071{_}The crows stuck a needle into her head and she was changed into a pigeon.
10085-8{_}5072{_}She took her flight to the house of the schoolmaster and perched upon a tree near by.
10085-8{_}5073{_}The people went to sow wheat.
10085-8{_}5074{_}"O master of the field," she said, "is H'ab Sliman yet hanged?"
10085-8{_}5075{_}She began to weep, and the rain fell until the end of the day's work.
10085-8{_}5076{_}One day the people of the village went to find a venerable old man and said to him:  "O old man, a bird is perched on one of our trees.
10085-8{_}5077{_}When we go to work the sky is covered with clouds and it rains.
10085-8{_}5078{_}When the day's work is done the sun shines."
10085-8{_}5079{_}"Go," said the old man, "put glue on the branch where it perches."
10085-8{_}5080{_}They put glue on its branch and caught the bird.
10085-8{_}5081{_}The daughter of the stepmother said to her mother:  "Let us kill it."
10085-8{_}5082{_}"No," said a slave, "we will amuse ourselves with it."
10085-8{_}5083{_}"No; kill it."
10085-8{_}5084{_}And they killed it.
10085-8{_}5085{_}Its blood spurted upon a rose-tree.
10085-8{_}5086{_}The rose-tree became so large that it overspread all the village.
10085-8{_}5087{_}The people worked to cut it down until evening, and yet it remained the size of a thread.
10085-8{_}5088{_}"To-morrow," they said, "we will finish it."
10085-8{_}5089{_}The next morning they found it as big as it was the day before.
10085-8{_}5090{_}They returned to the old man and said to him:  "O old man, we caught the bird and killed it.
10085-8{_}5091{_}Its blood gushed upon a rose-tree, which became so large that it overspreads the whole village.
10085-8{_}5092{_}Yesterday we worked all day to cut it down.
10085-8{_}5093{_}We left it the size of a thread.
10085-8{_}5094{_}This morning we find it as big as ever."
10085-8{_}5095{_}"O my children," said the old man, "you are not yet punished enough.
10085-8{_}5096{_}Take H'ab Sliman, perhaps he will have an expedient.
10085-8{_}5097{_}Make him sleep at your house."
10085-8{_}5098{_}H'ab Sliman said to them, "Give me a sickle."
10085-8{_}5099{_}Someone said to him: "We who are strong have cut all day without being able to accomplish it, and do you think you will be capable of it?
10085-8{_}5100{_}Let us see if you will find a new way to do it."
10085-8{_}5101{_}At the moment when he gave the first blow a voice said to him:  "Take care of me, O my brother!"
10085-8{_}5102{_}The voice wept, the child began to weep, and it rained.
10085-8{_}5103{_}H'ab Sliman recognized his sister.
10085-8{_}5104{_}"Laugh," he said.
10085-8{_}5105{_}She laughed and the sun shone, and the people got dried.
10085-8{_}5106{_}"Comb yourself," and legs of mutton fell.
10085-8{_}5107{_}All those who were present regaled themselves on them.
10085-8{_}5108{_}"Walk," and roses fell.
10085-8{_}5109{_}"But what is the matter with you, my sister?"
10085-8{_}5110{_}"What has happened to me."
10085-8{_}5111{_}"What revenge does your heart desire?"
10085-8{_}5112{_}"Attach the daughter of my stepmother to the tail of a horse that she may be dragged in the bushes."
10085-8{_}5113{_}When the young girl was dead, they took her to the house, cooked her, and sent her to her mother and sister.
10085-8{_}5114{_}"O my mother," cried the latter, "this eye is that of my sister Aftelis."
10085-8{_}5115{_}"Eat, unhappy one," said the mother, "your sister Aftelis has become the slave of slaves."
10085-8{_}5116{_}"But look at it," insisted the young girl.
10085-8{_}5117{_}"You have not even looked at it.
10085-8{_}5118{_}I will give this piece to the one who will weep a little."
10085-8{_}5119{_}"Well," said the cat, "if you give me that piece I will weep with one eye."
10085-8{_}5120{_}*       *       *       *       *   THE KING AND HIS SON   He had a son whom he brought up well.
10085-8{_}5121{_}The child grew and said one day to the King, "I am going out for a walk."
10085-8{_}5122{_}"It is well," answered the King.
10085-8{_}5123{_}At a certain place he found an olive-tree on fire.
10085-8{_}5124{_}"O God," he cried, "help me to put out this fire!"
10085-8{_}5125{_}Suddenly God sent the rain, the fire was extinguished, and the young man was able to pass.
10085-8{_}5126{_}He came to the city and said to the governor:  "Give me a chance to speak in my turn."
10085-8{_}5127{_}"It is well," said he; "speak."
10085-8{_}5128{_}"I ask the hand of your daughter," replied the young man.
10085-8{_}5129{_}"I give her to you," answered the governor, "for if you had not put out that fire the city would have been devoured by the flames."
10085-8{_}5130{_}He departed with his wife.
10085-8{_}5131{_}After a long march the wife made to God this prayer:  "O God, place this city here."
10085-8{_}5132{_}The city appeared at the very spot.
10085-8{_}5133{_}Toward evening the Marabout of the city of which the father of the young bridegroom was King went to the mosque to say his prayers.
10085-8{_}5134{_}"O marvel!"
10085-8{_}5135{_}he cried, "what do I see down there?"
10085-8{_}5136{_}The King called his wife and sent her to see what was this new city.
10085-8{_}5137{_}The woman departed, and, addressing the wife of the young prince, asked alms of him.
10085-8{_}5138{_}He gave her alms.
10085-8{_}5139{_}The messenger returned and said to the King:  "It is your son who commands in that city."
10085-8{_}5140{_}The King, pricked by jealousy, said to the woman: "Go, tell him to come and find me.
10085-8{_}5141{_}I must speak with him."
10085-8{_}5142{_}The woman went away and returned with the King's son.
10085-8{_}5143{_}His father said to him:  "If you are the son of the King, go and see your mother in the other world."
10085-8{_}5144{_}He regained his palace in tears.
10085-8{_}5145{_}"What is the matter with you," asked his wife, "you whom destiny has given me?"
10085-8{_}5146{_}He answered her: "My father told me, 'Go and see your mother in the other world.'"
10085-8{_}5147{_}"Return to your father," she replied, "and ask him for the book of the grandmother of your grandmother."
10085-8{_}5148{_}He returned to his father, who gave him the book.
10085-8{_}5149{_}He brought it to his wife, who said to him, "Lay it on the grave of your mother."
10085-8{_}5150{_}He placed it there and the grave opened.
10085-8{_}5151{_}He descended and found a man who was licking the earth.
10085-8{_}5152{_}He saw another who was eating mildew.
10085-8{_}5153{_}And he saw a third who was eating meat.
10085-8{_}5154{_}"Why do you eat meat?"
10085-8{_}5155{_}he asked him.
10085-8{_}5156{_}"Because I did good on earth," responded the shade.
10085-8{_}5157{_}"Where shall I find my mother?"
10085-8{_}5158{_}asked the prince.
10085-8{_}5159{_}The shade said, "She is down there."
10085-8{_}5160{_}He went to his mother, who asked him why he came to seek her.
10085-8{_}5161{_}He replied, "My father sent me."
10085-8{_}5162{_}"Return," said the mother, "and say to your father to lift up the beam which is on the hearth."
10085-8{_}5163{_}The prince went to his father.
10085-8{_}5164{_}"My mother bids you take up the beam which is above the hearth."
10085-8{_}5165{_}The King raised it and found a treasure.
10085-8{_}5166{_}"If you are the son of the King," he added, "bring me someone a foot high whose beard measures two feet."
10085-8{_}5167{_}The prince began to weep.
10085-8{_}5168{_}"Why do you weep," asked his wife, "you whom destiny has given me?"
10085-8{_}5169{_}The prince answered her, "My father said to me, 'Bring me someone a foot high whose beard measures two feet."
10085-8{_}5170{_}"Return to your father," she replied, "and ask him for the book of the grandfather of your grandfather."
10085-8{_}5171{_}His father gave him the book and the prince brought it to his wife.
10085-8{_}5172{_}"Take it to him again and let him put it in the assembly place, and call a public meeting."
10085-8{_}5173{_}A man a foot high appeared, took up the book, went around the city, and ate up all the inhabitants.
10085-8{_}5174{_}*       *       *       *       *   MAHOMET-BEN-SOLTAN  A certain sultan had a son who rode his horse through the city where his father reigned, and killed everyone he met.
10085-8{_}5175{_}The inhabitants united and promised a flock to him who should make him leave the city.
10085-8{_}5176{_}An old woman took it upon herself to realize the wishes of her fellow-citizens.
10085-8{_}5177{_}She procured some bladders and went to the fountain to fill them with the cup of an acorn.
10085-8{_}5178{_}The old man came to water his horse and said to the old woman:  "Get out of my way."
10085-8{_}5179{_}She would not move.
10085-8{_}5180{_}The young man rode his horse over the bladders and burst them.
10085-8{_}5181{_}"If you had married Thithbirth, a cavalier," cried the old woman, "you would not have done this damage.
10085-8{_}5182{_}But I predict that you will never marry her, for already seventy cavaliers have met death on her account."
10085-8{_}5183{_}The young man, pricked to the quick, regained his horse, took provisions, and set out for the place where he should find the young girl.
10085-8{_}5184{_}On the way he met a man.
10085-8{_}5185{_}They journeyed together.
10085-8{_}5186{_}Soon they perceived an ogress with a dead man at her side.
10085-8{_}5187{_}"Place him in the earth," said the ogress to them; "it is my son; the Sultan hanged him and cut off his foot with a sword."
10085-8{_}5188{_}They took one of the rings of the dead man and went on their way.
10085-8{_}5189{_}Soon they entered a village and offered the ring to the governor, who asked them for another like it.
10085-8{_}5190{_}They went away from there, returned through the country which they had traversed, and met a pilgrim who had made the tour of the world.
10085-8{_}5191{_}They had visited every place except the sea.
10085-8{_}5192{_}They turned toward the sea.
10085-8{_}5193{_}At the moment of embarking, a whale barred their passage.
10085-8{_}5194{_}They retraced their steps, and met the ogress, took a second ring from the dead man, and departed.
10085-8{_}5195{_}At a place they found sixty corpses.
10085-8{_}5196{_}A singing bird was guarding them.
10085-8{_}5197{_}The travellers stopped and heard the bird say:  "He who shall speak here shall be changed into a rock and shall die.
10085-8{_}5198{_}Mahomet-ben-Soltan, you shall never wed the young girl.
10085-8{_}5199{_}Ninety-nine cavaliers have already met death on her account."
10085-8{_}5200{_}Mahomet stayed till morning without saying one word.
10085-8{_}5201{_}Then he departed with his companion for the city where Thithbirth dwelt.
10085-8{_}5202{_}When they arrived they were pressed with hunger.
10085-8{_}5203{_}Mahomet's companion said to him:  "Sing that which you heard the bird sing."
10085-8{_}5204{_}He began to sing.
10085-8{_}5205{_}The young girl, whom they meant to buy, heard him and asked him from whom he had got that song.
10085-8{_}5206{_}"From my head," he answered.
10085-8{_}5207{_}Mahomet's companion said: "We learned it in the fields from a singing bird."
10085-8{_}5208{_}"Bring me that bird," she said, "or I'll have your head cut off."
10085-8{_}5209{_}Mahomet took a lantern and a cage which he placed upon the branch of the tree where the bird was perching.
10085-8{_}5210{_}"Do you think to catch me?"
10085-8{_}5211{_}cried the bird.
10085-8{_}5212{_}The next day it entered the cage and the young man took it away.
10085-8{_}5213{_}When they were in the presence of the young girl the bird said to her:  "We have come to buy you."
10085-8{_}5214{_}The father of the young girl said to Mahomet: "If you find her you may have her.
10085-8{_}5215{_}But if not, I will kill you.
10085-8{_}5216{_}Ninety-nine cavaliers have already met death thus.
10085-8{_}5217{_}You will be the hundredth."
10085-8{_}5218{_}The bird flew toward the woman.
10085-8{_}5219{_}"Where shall I find you?"
10085-8{_}5220{_}it asked her.
10085-8{_}5221{_}She answered: "You see that door at which I am sitting; it is the usual place of my father.
10085-8{_}5222{_}I shall be hidden underneath."
10085-8{_}5223{_}The next day Mahomet presented himself before the Sultan: "Arise," he said, "your daughter is hidden there."
10085-8{_}5224{_}The Sultan imposed this new condition: "My daughter resembles ninety-nine others of her age.
10085-8{_}5225{_}She is the hundredth.
10085-8{_}5226{_}If you recognize her in the group I will give her to you.
10085-8{_}5227{_}But if not, I will kill you."
10085-8{_}5228{_}The young girl said to Mahomet, "I will ride a lame horse."
10085-8{_}5229{_}Mahomet recognized her, and the Sultan gave her to him, with a serving-maid, a female slave, and another woman.
10085-8{_}5230{_}Mahomet and his companion departed.
10085-8{_}5231{_}Arriving at a certain road they separated.
10085-8{_}5232{_}Mahomet retained for himself his wife and the slave woman, and gave to his companion the two other women.
10085-8{_}5233{_}He gained the desert and left for a moment his wife and the slave woman.
10085-8{_}5234{_}In his absence an ogre took away his wife.
10085-8{_}5235{_}He ran in search of her and met some shepherds.
10085-8{_}5236{_}"O shepherds," he said, "can you tell me where the ogre lives?"
10085-8{_}5237{_}They pointed out the place.
10085-8{_}5238{_}Arriving, he saw his wife.
10085-8{_}5239{_}Soon the ogre appeared, and Mahomet asked where he should find his destiny.
10085-8{_}5240{_}"My destiny is far from here," answered the ogre.
10085-8{_}5241{_}"My destiny is in an egg, the egg in a pigeon, the pigeon in a camel, the camel in the sea."
10085-8{_}5242{_}Mahomet arose, ran to dig a hole at the shore of the sea, stretched a mat over the hole; a camel sprang from the water and fell into the hole.
10085-8{_}5243{_}He killed it and took out an egg, crushed the egg in his hands, and the ogre died.
10085-8{_}5244{_}Mahomet took his wife and came to his father's city, where he built himself a palace.
10085-8{_}5245{_}The father promised a flock to him who should kill his son.
10085-8{_}5246{_}As no one offered, he sent an army of soldiers to besiege him.
10085-8{_}5247{_}He called one of them in particular and said to him:  "Kill Mahomet and I will enrich you."
10085-8{_}5248{_}The soldiers managed to get near the young prince, put out his eyes, and left him in the field.
10085-8{_}5249{_}An eagle passed and said to Mahomet: "Don't do any good to your parents, but since your father has made you blind take the bark of this tree, apply it to your eyes, and you will be cured."
10085-8{_}5250{_}The young man was healed.
10085-8{_}5251{_}A short time after his father said to him, "I will wed your wife."
10085-8{_}5252{_}"You cannot," he answered.
10085-8{_}5253{_}The Sultan convoked the Marabout, who refused him the dispensation he demanded.
10085-8{_}5254{_}Soon Mahomet killed his father and celebrated his wedding-feast for seven days and seven nights.
